Interpretation of 'Wajh' and Refutation of Ash'ari View
Sanusi interprets 'wajh' as existence, rejects Ash'ari attribute view, and gives evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi interprets 'wajh' as existence (wujud) rather than as an attribute, and the evidence he provides from the Quranic verse.

Core Idea
The 'face' of Allah is His existence, not a literal attribute.

Sanusi engages with a key Quranic verse often cited by anthropomorphists. He clarifies that 'wajh' means Allah's existence (wujud), not a separate attribute. This lesson examines his reasoning, including his critique of the Ash'ari position and the grammatical evidence from the verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and passage
Read the Arabic verse and the passage slowly. Note the two interpretations: 'wajh' as existence vs. as an attribute.
2
Understand the first argument
Sanusi argues that attributes are not specifically characterized by remaining (baqa'). Consider why this makes the attribute interpretation problematic.
The forced response (takalluf) is mentioned as a weak counterargument.
3
Understand the second argument
The verse describes 'wajh' as 'Owner of Majesty and Honor'. Analyse why an attribute cannot be described by another attribute, leading to the conclusion that 'wajh' refers to the essence.
Majesty (jalal) pertains to the attributes of lordship, which belong to the essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ( الوجه ( في قولِهِ تعالى : ( وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الْجَلَلِ وَالْإِكْرَامِ ) الرحمن : ۲۷] : فأوَّلَهُ الإمام بالوجود ؛ أي : ويبقى وجود ربَّكَ ذو الجلال والإكرام ، وهو ذاته سبحانَهُ ، ويبعد حمْلُ الوجه على صفةٍ من صفاتِهِ تعالى كما يقوله الشيخ الأشعري ؛ لعدم اختصاص صفتِهِ تعالى بالبقاء (۱) وعبارته في الإبانة في القطعة المأمونة التي رواها الحافظ ابن عساكر في تبيين كذب المفتري (ص ۳۱۹): (وأن له وجهاً كما قال: ﴿ وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الْجَلَالِ وَالْإِكْرَامِ ﴾) . بل هو جلَّ وعلا الواجب القدم والبقاء بذاتِهِ وجميعِ صفاتِهِ ، إلا أنْ يُجابَ لهُ بأنَّ بقاء الصفةِ يستلزم بقاء الموصوفِ وسائرِ صفاتِهِ ، وفيهِ معَ ذلكَ تكلُّفٌ وممَّا يدلُّ أيضاً على أنَّ المراد بـ ( الوجهِ ( الوجودُ : نعتُهُ بأَنَّهُ ذو الجلال والإكرام ، والموصوفُ بالجلالِ هو الله سبحانه وتعالى ؛ لأنَّ الجلال هو صفاتِ الربوبية ، فلو أُريد بـ ( الوجهِ ) صفةٌ مِنْ صفاتِهِ تعالى .. لم يُتصوَّرْ أَنْ تُوصف بصفاتٍ ؛ إذ الصفة لا تقوم بها صفةٌ .
As for 'the face' in His statement, Exalted is He: 'And there will remain the Face of your Lord, Owner of Majesty and Honor' [ar-Rahman 55:27]: the Imam interpreted it as existence; i.e., 'the existence of your Lord, Owner of Majesty and Honor, will remain,' and it is His essence, glorified be He. And it is unlikely to interpret 'the face' as one of His attributes, Exalted is He, as Shaykh al-Ash'ari says, because His attribute is not specifically characterized by remaining. (1) His expression in al-Ibana in the reliable portion narrated by al-Hafiz Ibn 'Asakir in Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari (p. 319): 'And that He has a face as He said: And there will remain the Face of your Lord, Owner of Majesty and Honor.' Rather, He, Glorified and Exalted, is the necessarily preeternal and everlasting in His essence and all His attributes. However, it could be answered for him that the remaining of the attribute entails the remaining of the described and the rest of His attributes, but that is still forced. And among what also indicates that what is meant by 'the face' is existence: His description of it as 'Owner of Majesty and Honor,' and the one described by majesty is Allah, glorified be He and Exalted; because majesty is the attributes of lordship. So if what is meant by 'the face' were an attribute of His attributes, Exalted is He, it could not be conceived that it be described by attributes, for an attribute does not subsist by an attribute.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument about the interpretation of the word 'wajh' (face) in the Quranic verse 'Yabqa Wajhu Rabbika'. The author, Sanusi, states that the Imam (likely a reference to a leading scholar) interpreted 'wajh' as existence (wujud), meaning that the verse says: 'the existence of your Lord will remain,' and that existence is identical to His essence. He then critiques the Ash'ari interpretation which takes 'wajh' as one of God's attributes, on the grounds that no attribute is specifically characterized by remaining (baqa'), rather God is necessarily preeternal and everlasting in His essence and all His attributes. Sanusi acknowledges that one could respond by saying that the remaining of the attribute entails the remaining of the described and the rest of His attributes, but he considers this response forced (takalluf). He then provides additional evidence for his interpretation: the verse describes the 'face' as 'Owner of Majesty and Honor' (dhu al-jalali wa al-ikram). Majesty (jalal) is a description of the attributes of lordship, which belong to God's essence. If 'face' were an attribute, it could not itself be described by attributes, because an attribute cannot subsist by another attribute. Thus, 'face' must refer to the essence (existence) itself.

الوجه
الوجود
صفات الله
الأشعرية
الإبانة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'wajh' is a literal face or a separate attribute of God.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that 'wajh' means existence (wujud) or essence, not a separate attribute. He provides two arguments: attributes are not specifically characterized by remaining, and an attribute cannot be described by another attribute as 'wajh' is described in the verse.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the Ash'ari interpretation that 'wajh' is an attribute of God?
A) Because an attribute cannot remain by itself.
B) Because God's attributes are not eternal.
C) Because 'wajh' is described as having attributes, which an attribute cannot have.
D) Because the Imam interpreted it as existence.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi argues that 'wajh' in the verse refers to Allah's existence (essence), not a separate attribute, based on the impossibility of an attribute being described by another attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Are you attached to worldly things that will perish, while Allah's essence alone remains? How does the verse's emphasis on the everlastingness of His existence confront your priorities today?

Why God's Life Was Delayed and the Proof of Pre-Eternity
Sanusi justifies delaying life discussion and adds proofs of pre-eternity and permanence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the methodological reason for delaying the discussion of God's life in kalam works and how the proof of pre-eternity and permanence is added as a completion.

Core Idea
Life is a condition for other attributes, so it is proven through them first.

Sanusi explains why the discussion of God's life was postponed to this chapter. He shows that the previous attributes, classified as qualitative attributes, are conditioned by life. Since the existence of a conditioned thing indicates its condition, those earlier discussions serve as evidence for life. Then he adds proofs of pre-eternity and permanence for all attributes to complete the benefit.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify its structure
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the two main sections: the reason for delaying life and the addition of proofs of pre-eternity and permanence.
2
Understand the conditioned-condition logic
The author argues that the previous attributes (الصفات المعنوية) are conditioned by life. Their existence proves life's existence because a conditioned thing implies its condition.
This is a key logical principle in kalam: knowledge of the evidence precedes knowledge of the evidenced.
3
Follow the sequence of chapters
Since knowledge of the evidence comes first, the earlier chapters (on other attributes) were placed before this chapter on life. This ordering is intentional to present evidence before the evidenced.
4
Reflect on the added benefit
The author says he adds proofs of pre-eternity (قدم) and permanence (بقاء) for all attributes here, even though earlier chapters already hinted at the evidence. This is to complete the benefit.
Think about why proving these additional aspects is important for the overall theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفضل الخامس في وجوب حياته تعالى واقامته براهین قاطعة على وجوب القدم والبقاء بجميع ما نتصف به ذات مولانا جل وعز وأنه يتعالى عن الاتصاف با سحوادث إنَّما أَخَّرَ الكلامَ في الحياةِ إلى هذا الفصل ; لأنَّ ما سبقَ مِنَ الصفات المعنوية والمعاني كلُّ واحدٍ منها يصلحُ أنْ يُستدَلَّ به على ثبوتِ الحياة ; لأنَّ ثبوتهُ مشروط بثبوتها ، وثبوت المشروط دليل على ثبوتِ شرطه ، والعلمُ بالدليل سابقٌ على العلم بالمدلول ، فتقديم تلكَ الفصول على هذا الفصلِ مِنْ بابِ تقديم الدليل على المدلول ثم أضاف إلى ثبوتِ الحياة في هاذا الفصل إثبات القدمِ والبقاء لجميعِ الصفات التي تقوم بذاتِ مولانا جلَّ وعزَّ ; تكميلاً للفائدة ، وإلا فقد تقدَّمَ في الفصولِ السابقة ما يرشد إلى دليل ذلك ، وبالله التوفيق .
The fifth chapter: On the necessity of His life, Exalted is He, and establishing conclusive proofs for the necessity of pre-eternity and permanence for all that the essence of our Master, Mighty and Majestic, is described with, and that He is exalted above being described with [؟] events. He only delayed the discussion of life to this chapter because the previous [attributes] from the qualitative attributes and meanings, each one of them can be used as evidence for the establishment of life; because its establishment is conditional upon its establishment, and the establishment of the conditioned is evidence for the establishment of its condition, and knowledge of the evidence precedes knowledge of the evidenced. Thus the presentation of those chapters before this chapter is of the type of presenting the evidence before the evidenced. Then he added to the establishment of life in this chapter the proof of pre-eternity and permanence for all the attributes that subsist in the essence of our Master, Mighty and Majestic, as a completion of benefit; otherwise, what guides to the evidence for that has already preceded in the previous chapters. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage introduces the fifth chapter on the necessity of God's life (حياة) and establishes conclusive proofs for His pre-eternity (قدم) and permanence (بقاء) for all attributes of His essence. The author explains why the discussion of life was postponed to this chapter: because the previously discussed attributes (الصفات المعنوية) are each conditioned by life; the existence of a conditioned thing indicates the existence of its condition. Since knowledge of the evidence precedes knowledge of the evidenced, the earlier chapters served as evidence for life. Then, in this chapter, the author adds proof of pre-eternity and permanence for all attributes to complete the benefit, although the earlier chapters already hinted at the evidence. The passage ends with a plea for divine success.

Misconception: Some might think that the existence of God's life is proven independently, without relying on other attributes.
Correction: The passage shows that life is proven through the conditioned-condition relationship: the existence of other attributes (conditioned) indicates the existence of life (condition). Thus, life is inferred from them, not proven in isolation.

Proof of God's Life, Eternity, and Permanence
Sanusi proves God's life and extends it to eternity and permanence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi proves God's life from the necessity of other attributes and extends the proof to show that life is eternal and permanent.

Core Idea
God's life is inferred from His other attributes; it must be eternal and permanent.

Sanusi delays the discussion of God's life to the fifth chapter because the other attributes (knowledge, power, etc.) serve as evidence for life. Once life is proven, he applies the same reasoning to show that life itself must be eternal and permanent. This lesson unpacks that logical chain.

Guided Path
1
Understand the delay in presentation
Read the opening explanation: why is life discussed after other attributes? Sanusi argues that the other attributes are conditioned by life, so they are evidence for life. Evidence should precede the evidenced.
This is a pedagogical choice, not a theological ranking.
2
Follow the proof for life
Identify the core proof: God must be living because otherwise He could not have the attributes (knowledge, power, etc.) that have already been proven necessary. Their existence is conditioned by life; if life were absent, they would be absent—but they are not absent, so life exists.
This is a conditional proof: if no life, then no attributes; but attributes are necessary, so life is necessary.
3
Extend to eternity and permanence
Notice how Sanusi argues that life must be eternal (qadim) and permanent (baqi). Since the attributes conditioned by life are eternal, their condition (life) cannot be temporal. The text cuts off, but the logic is that if life were temporal, the conditioned attributes would also be temporal, contradicting their proven eternity.
The proof is incomplete in the text, but the direction is clear.
4
Reflect on the interconnectedness
Ask yourself: how does this proof show the unity of divine attributes? Each attribute supports the others, and the whole is consistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفضل الخامس في وجوب حياته تعالى واقامته براهين قاطعة على وجوب القدم والبقاء بجميع ما نتصف به ذات مولانا جل وعز وأنه يتعالى عن الاتصاف بالحوادث إنما أخر الكلام في الحياة إلى هذا الفصل؛ لأن ما سبق من الصفات المعنوية والمعاني كل واحد منها يصلح أن يستدل به على ثبوت الحياة؛ لأن ثبوته مشروط بثبوتها، وثبوت المشروط دليل على ثبوت شرطه، والعلم بالدليل سابق على العلم بالمدلول، فتقديم تلك الفصول على هذا الفصل من باب تقديم الدليل على المدلول ثم أضاف إلى ثبوت الحياة في هذا الفصل إثبات القدم والبقاء لجميع الصفات التي تقوم بذات مولانا جل وعز؛ تكميلا للفائدة، وإلا فقد تقدم في الفصول السابقة ما يرشد إلى دليل ذلك، وبالله التوفيق. ويلزم أن يكون تعالى حيا، وإلا لم يتصف بعلم ولا قدرة ولا إرادة ولا سمع ولا بصر ولا كلام، بحياة قديمة؛ لما سبق من وجوب قدم مشروطها، يستحيل تأخره عن مشروطه، واجبة البقاء، وإلا لانتفى قدمها، وقد عرفت الآن وجوبه والشرط يعني: أنه يستدل على ثبوت الحياة له تعالى بما عرفت وجوبه له جل وعز من صفات المعاني؛ كالعلم والقدرة ونحوهما ووجه الاستدلال بها: أن ثبوتها مشروط عقلا بثبوت الحياة؛ فلو انتفت الحياة لانتف تلك الصفات التي قام البرهان على وجوبها له جل وعلا، ولما تقرر أن عدم الشرط يستلزم عدم المشروط، لكن نفي تلك الصفات الواجبة مستحيل، فنفي شرطها الذي هو الحياة مستحيل. ومن هنا تعرف وجوب القدم والبقاء لحياته تعالى؛ إذ هما واجبان لأن تلك الصفات المشروطة بالحياة قد سبق وجوب قدمها، فلو كانت
The fifth chapter on the necessity of His life, may He be exalted, and establishing conclusive proofs for the necessity of pre-eternity and permanence for all that the essence of our Master, may He be glorified and exalted, is described with, and that He is exalted above being described with temporal events. He only delayed the discussion of life to this chapter because the previous chapters on the essential attributes (sifat ma'nawiyya) and meanings (ma'ani) — each one of them is suitable to be used as evidence for the affirmation of life; because its affirmation is conditioned by its affirmation, and the affirmation of the conditioned is evidence for the affirmation of its condition, and knowledge of the evidence precedes knowledge of the evidenced. Thus, placing those chapters before this chapter is in the manner of placing the evidence before the evidenced. Then he added to the affirmation of life in this chapter the affirmation of pre-eternity and permanence for all the attributes that subsist in the essence of our Master, may He be glorified and exalted, as a completion of benefit; otherwise, the previous chapters already contain what guides to the proof of that. And with Allah is success. And it follows necessarily that He, exalted, be living; otherwise He would not be described with knowledge, power, will, hearing, sight, or speech, with a pre-eternal life; because of what preceded of the necessity of the pre-eternity of its conditioned, it being impossible for it to be delayed from its condition, and it is necessarily permanent; otherwise its pre-eternity would be negated. And you have now known its necessity. And the condition means: that one proves the affirmation of life for Him, exalted, by what you have known to be necessary for Him, glorified and exalted, from the attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma'ani), such as knowledge, power, and the like. And the way of inference from them is that their affirmation is rationally conditioned by the affirmation of life; so if life were negated, those attributes which the proof established as necessary for Him, glorified and exalted, would be negated. And since it is established that the absence of the condition necessitates the absence of the conditioned, but the negation of those necessary attributes is impossible, so the negation of their condition, which is life, is impossible. And from here you know the necessity of pre-eternity and permanence for His life, may He be exalted; for they are both necessary because those attributes conditioned by life have already been proven necessary in their pre-eternity. For if they were...
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a proof and its extension. Sanusi first explains why the discussion of God's life (hayat) was delayed to the fifth chapter: because the attributes previously discussed (such as knowledge, power) serve as evidence for life, since their existence is conditioned by life. Presenting the evidence before the evidenced is the proper order. He then adds the proof that life itself is eternal (qadim) and permanent (baqi), completing the benefit. The proof for life itself is as follows: God must be living, otherwise He could not possess the attributes (knowledge, power, will, hearing, sight, speech) that have already been proven necessary. These attributes are conditioned by life; if life were absent, they would be absent. But their absence is impossible, so life is necessary. Furthermore, life must be eternal and permanent. The attributes conditioned by life have already been proven eternal; if life were temporal, it would be possible for its eternity to be negated, but the conditioned cannot be separated from its condition. The text ends mid-sentence, but the intended argument is that if life were not eternal, the conditioned attributes would also not be eternal, contradicting their proven eternity.

Key Terms
حياة
قدم
بقاء
مشروط
شرط
صفات المعاني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's life is proven separately and independently from other attributes.
Correction: Sanusi shows that life is inferred from the other attributes because they are conditioned by life. The proof is indirect: since the conditioned exists, the condition must exist.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi delay the discussion of God's life to a later chapter?
A) Because life is less important than other attributes.
B) Because the other attributes serve as evidence for life, and evidence should precede the evidenced.
C) Because life is a temporal attribute that requires prior discussion of temporality.
D) Because the author forgot to include it earlier.

Key Takeaway
God's life is proven indirectly from the necessity of other attributes; it must be eternal and permanent because the conditioned cannot be separated from its condition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's life is the condition for all His attributes, and your own life is entirely dependent on His life, are you living with the constant awareness that you are held in existence by Him every moment? What is one habit you can adopt this week to remind yourself of this dependence?
?
The proof shows that denying God's life would mean denying His knowledge and power. Have you ever acted as if God was not fully aware of your thoughts or actions? What must you change today to align your heart with the reality that His life entails complete knowledge of you?
?
Since God's life is eternal and permanent, your relationship with Him must be anchored in an unchanging reality. Are you building your life on temporary things that will fade, or on the eternal life of God? What step will you take this week to shift your foundation?

Proof for the Attribute of Life and Its Eternity
Sanusi proves God's life as necessary, eternal, and everlasting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi proves that God's attribute of life is necessary, eternal, and everlasting through logical conditionality with the other attributes.

Core Idea
Life is the rational condition for all other divine attributes; its necessity and eternity follow from theirs.

Sanusi established earlier that God possesses attributes like knowledge and power. Here, he proves that these attributes require life as their precondition. Using the logical relationship between condition and conditioned, he demonstrates that life must exist, be eternal, and never cease.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's rhythm and argument structure come through.
Notice the recurring terms 'shart' (condition) and 'mashrut' (conditioned).
2
Identify the main claim
The passage asserts that God must be living (hayy). Find the sentence that states this directly and note how it is framed as a necessary consequence.
The claim is: 'It necessarily follows that He be living.'
3
Understand the conditional argument
Trace the logic: Life is a condition for attributes like knowledge and power. Since those attributes are proven necessary, their condition (life) must also exist. The absence of life would entail the absence of those necessary attributes, which is impossible.
The argument uses the principle: absence of condition implies absence of conditioned.
4
Extend to eternity and permanence
Notice how Sanusi uses the same conditional relationship to establish that life must be eternal (qadim) and permanent (baqi). The conditioned attributes are eternal, so their condition cannot be originated. And what is eternal cannot cease.
This step shows how a single proof yields multiple conclusions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليلُ ثبوتِ صفةِ الحياةِ لهُ تعالى : ويلزمُ أنْ يكونَ تعالى حيّاً ، وإلا لم يتّصف بعلم ولا قدرة ولا إرادة ولا سمع ولا بصر ولا كلام ، بحياة قديمةٍ ؛ لما سبقَ مِنْ وجوبِ قِدَمِ مشروطها ، يستحيلُ تأخُّرُهُ عن مشروطِهِ ، واجبة البقاء ، وإلا لانتفى قدمها ، وقد عرفت الآنَ وجوبَهُ والشرط يعني : أَنَّهُ يُستدَلُّ على ثبوتِ الحياةِ لهُ تعالى بما عرفت وجوبَهُ لهُ جل وعزَّ مِنْ صفاتِ المعاني ؛ كالعلم والقدرة ونحوهما ووجه الاستدلال بها : أنَّ ثبوتها مشروط عقلاً بثبوتِ الحياة ؛ فلو انتفَتِ الحياة لانتفَتْ تلك الصفاتُ التي قام البرهان على وجوبها له جلَّ وعلا ، ولما تقرَّرَ أنَّ عدمَ الشرط يستلزم عدم المشروط ، لكنَّ نفْيَ تلك الصفاتِ الواجبة مستحيل ، فنفي شرطها الذي هو الحياةُ مستحيل . ومن هنا تعرفُ وجوب القدم والبقاء لحياتِهِ تعالى ؛ إذ هما واجبانِ أنَّ المشروطها ، والمشروط لا يفارقُ شرطَه ، وبعبارة أخرى ؛ وهي تلك الصفاتِ المشروطة بالحياة قد سبق وجوب قدمها ، فلو كانَتِ الحياة التي هي شرط فيها حادثةً . . لزمَ تأخَّرُ الشرط عن المشروط ، وهو مستحيل ، وإذا عرفت وجوب القدم لحياتِهِ تعالى عرفت وجوبَ بقائها ؛ لِمَا سبق برهانهُ مِنْ أنَّ ما ثبت قدمُهُ استحال عدمه ، فلو جازَ أنْ يطراً العدمُ على حياتِهِ تعالى بموت ونحوه . . لانتفى قدمها ، وهو واجب لها ؛ لما عرفت الآن . وتقرير دليلِ قِدَمِ الحياةِ وبقائها بهذه العبارة.. أسعد بلفظ العقيدة (١) ، وبالله تعالى التوفيقُ .
Proof of the affirmation of the attribute of life for Him, exalted is He: It necessarily follows that He, exalted is He, be living, otherwise He would not be described with knowledge, nor power, nor will, nor hearing, nor sight, nor speech, with an eternal life; because of what preceded of the necessity of the eternity of its conditioned (mashrut), it is impossible for it [the condition] to be delayed from its conditioned; and it is necessary in permanence (baqa'), otherwise its eternity (qidam) would be negated, and you have now known its necessity. And 'the condition' means: that one argues for the affirmation of life for Him, exalted is He, by what you have known is necessary for Him, mighty and majestic, from the attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma'ani), such as knowledge, power, and their like. And the way of argumentation by them is: that their affirmation is rationally conditioned by the affirmation of life; so if life were negated, those attributes whose necessity for Him, mighty and exalted, has been proven by demonstration would be negated; and since it is established that the absence of the condition necessitates the absence of the conditioned, but the negation of those necessary attributes is impossible, so the negation of their condition, which is life, is impossible. And from this you know the necessity of eternity (qidam) and permanence (baqa') for His life; for both are necessary for its conditioned, and the conditioned does not separate from its condition. In other words, these attributes conditioned by life have already had the necessity of their eternity established, so if life, which is their condition, were originated, then the condition would be delayed from the conditioned, which is impossible. And if you know the necessity of eternity for His life, you know the necessity of its permanence, due to what its proof has preceded: that what is established in eternity is impossible to cease. So if it were possible for non-existence to occur to His life through death or the like, its eternity would be negated, and it is necessary for it, as you have now known. And the formulation of the proof of the eternity of life and its permanence in this wording is most felicitous with the wording of the creed. And by Allah, exalted, is success.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is a proof for God's attribute of life and its necessary properties. The author begins by stating that God must be living (hayy), because otherwise He could not possess the attributes of knowledge, power, will, hearing, sight, and speech—all of which have already been proven necessary for God. Life is thus a precondition for these attributes. The proof proceeds by noting that the existence of these attributes is rationally conditioned by life; if life were absent, they would be absent, but since their existence is necessary, their condition (life) must also exist. From this, the author deduces that life must be eternal (qadim) and everlasting (baqi). The argument for eternity: the conditioned (the other attributes) are eternal, and the condition cannot be posterior to the conditioned, so life must also be eternal. For permanence: once something is established as eternal, it cannot cease to exist; otherwise it would not have been eternal. The passage ends by noting that this formulation aligns with creedal statements.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think life is merely a metaphor or not a real attribute; this proof establishes it as a necessary, real, and eternal attribute based on logical conditionality.
Correction: The passage shows that life is a real attribute (sifat al-ma'ani) because it serves as a rational condition for other real attributes. Without life, those attributes would be impossible, but they are proven necessary, so life is also necessary.

Proof of the Eternity and Permanence of God's Life
Sanusi proves the pre-eternity and permanence of God's life using two linked arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's dual proof that God's attribute of life is both pre-eternal (qadim) and permanent (baqi).

Core Idea
Life must be eternal and never ending, for what is pre-eternal cannot cease.

In this passage, Sanusi presents a concise argument for two related aspects of God's attribute of life: its pre-eternity (qidam) and its permanence (baqa'). The first part uses a conditional to show that life cannot be contingent but must be pre-eternal. The second part builds on that to show that since life is pre-eternal, it cannot later cease to exist. Together, these establish the uncreated and everlasting nature of God's life.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get a sense of the argument.
Notice the logical structure: 'if...then...impossible'.
2
Understand the conditional argument for pre-eternity
Identify that life is presented as a condition (shart) for something. If it were contingent, the condition would come after the conditioned (mashrut), which is impossible. Therefore life must be pre-eternal.
The impossibility is key: a condition cannot be later than what it conditions.
3
Understand the argument for permanence
Since life is pre-eternal, it cannot cease to exist. If non-existence could occur, pre-eternity would be negated.
This relies on the principle: what is pre-eternal cannot cease.
4
Reflect on the author's concluding note
Sanusi comments that this formulation is more appropriate for the creed (aqida). This signals the importance of precise wording in theological proofs.
The phrase 'أسعد بلفظ العقيدة' indicates his methodological awareness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحياة التي هي شرط فيها حادثةً . . لزمَ تأخَّرُ الشرط عن المشروط ، وهو مستحيل ، وإذا عرفت وجوب القدم لحياتِهِ تعالى عرفت وجوبَ بقائها ؛ لِمَا سبق برهانهُ مِنْ أنَّ ما ثبت قدمُهُ استحال عدمه ، فلو جازَ أنْ يطراً العدمُ على حياتِهِ تعالى بموت ونحوه . . لانتفى قدمها ، وهو واجب لها ؛ لما عرفت الآن . وتقرير دليلِ قِدَمِ الحياةِ وبقائها بهذه العبارة.. أسعد بلفظ العقيدة ، وبالله تعالى التوفيقُ .
If life, which is a condition in it, were contingent, then the condition would be delayed from the conditioned, and that is impossible. And if you have known the necessity of pre-eternity (qidam) for His life, may He be exalted, you have known the necessity of its permanence (baqa') because of what has previously been proven: that what is established as pre-eternal is impossible to cease to exist. For if non-existence were to occur to His life, may He be exalted, by death or the like, then its pre-eternity would be negated, while it is necessary for it, as you have now come to know. The formulation of the proof for the pre-eternity of life and its permanence in this expression is more felicitous (as'ad) with the wording of the Creed, and with God Almighty is success.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage is a proof establishing the pre-eternity (qidam) and permanence (baqa') of God's attribute of life. The author begins by stating a conditional: if life were contingent (haditha), then the condition (shart) would be posterior to the conditioned (mashrut), which is impossible. Here 'life' is presented as a condition for something unspecified (likely for knowledge, power, etc., as in the broader context). The impossibility of the condition being later than the conditioned shows life must be pre-eternal. Then, because it is pre-eternal, it must also be permanent (cannot cease), since anything pre-eternal cannot accept non-existence by logical necessity. If non-existence (death or similar) could occur to God's life, that would imply life was not pre-eternal in the first place. The proof is concise and relies on the principle that what is pre-eternal cannot cease. The author ends by saying this formulation of the proof is more appropriate for the creed (aqida) and seeks God's help.

God's Attributes are All Eternal and Permanent
Sanusi presents a general proof for the pre-eternity of all divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proof that all of God's attributes are pre-eternal and cannot be contingent, based on the impossibility of the essence accepting new attributes.

Core Idea
God's attributes are all eternal; the essence cannot accept temporal attributes.

Sanusi now provides a general proof that all attributes of God, not just those we know, are eternal and permanent. The argument uses a reductio: if any attribute were contingent, it would entail an impossibility. This lesson walks through that proof and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get a sense of the argument's flow.
Pay attention to the logical connectors like 'if' and 'then'.
2
Follow the reductio argument
The argument begins by supposing an attribute could accept non-existence. Identify the steps that lead to contradiction.
3
Understand the infinite regress argument
If the essence's receptivity to a contingent attribute were itself contingent, it would require another receptivity, leading to infinite regress.
This shows that receptivity must be pre-eternal.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The proof concludes that all attributes subsisting in God are eternal and necessary, and no attribute can arise later.
This reinforces that God is not a locus for temporal events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فضل في أحكام الصفات
1 صفات المعاني متصفةٌ كلُّها بالقدم والبقاء ]
وكذا يجب القدمُ والبقاء لسائر الصفاتِ التي تقوم بذاتِهِ تعالى ؛ إذْ لو قبلَتِ العدمَ لكانَتْ حادثة ؛ لِمَا عرفْتَ أَنَّ القديم لا يقبلُ العدم، وهو تعالى يستحيلُ أنْ يتّصف بصفةٍ حادثة ، وإلا لكانَتْ ذاتُهُ قابلة لها في الأزلِ ؛ لأنَّ قبوله لها نفسي ، ولو كانَ أيضاً حادثاً للذاتِ . . لاحتاجَتِ الذات إلى قبول آخر لذلك القبول ، ويتسلسل
وإذا لزمَ أنْ يكونَ قبولُهُ لتلك الصفة المفروضة الحدوثِ كائناً في الأزلِ .. صح أنْ يتّصفَ بتلك الصفة الحادثة في الأزلِ ؛ إذْ لا معنى للقبولِ إلا ذلك ، وذلكَ محال ؛ إذ الحادث لا يمكن أن يكون قديماً ، لأنَّ مِنْ لازم القديم ألا يقبل العدمَ ، والحادث قد قبل العدمَ واتَّصفَ بهِ ، فهما
متنافيان
فخرجَ لكَ بهذا : أنَّ كلَّ ما قبلَتْهُ الذاتُ العليَّةُ مِنَ الصفات فهو أزلي واجب لها ، لا يُتصوَّرُ أنْ يكونَ حادثاً وما لم تقبله الذاتُ العليَّةُ في الأزلِ فلا تقبله أبداً ؛ لِمَا عرفْتَ مِن استحالةِ أنْ يطرأ القبول على الذاتِ بعدَ أنْ لم
يكن لها
لمَّا بَيَّنَ بالبرهان وجوبَ القدم والبقاء للحياة ولما قبلها مِنَ الصفات التي عرفنا بالعقل وبالشرع اتصافَهُ تعالى بها .. أرادَ أَنْ يُبيِّنَ هنا بالبرهان وجوبَ القدم والبقاء لسائر الصفات التي تقوم بذاتِهِ تعالى عموماً ، ما عرفناه منها وما لم نعرفه ، بحيثُ نقطعُ باستحالة أن تكونَ الذات العليَّةُ محلاً للحوادثِ ، وأنَّها لا تتصفُ إلا بصفة واجبة القدم
والبقاء .
A chapter on the rulings of attributes.
[1] All attributes of meaning (sifat al-ma'ani) are characterized by pre-eternity and permanence.
Likewise, pre-eternity and permanence are necessary for all other attributes that subsist in His essence, may He be exalted; for if they accepted non-existence, they would be contingent, since you know that the pre-eternal does not accept non-existence. And it is impossible for Him, may He be exalted, to be characterized by a contingent attribute; otherwise, His essence would be receptive to it in pre-eternity, because its receptivity is essential (nafsi). And if it were also contingent for the essence, then the essence would need another receptivity for that receptivity, leading to infinite regress. And if it is necessary that His receptivity to that supposed contingent attribute be in pre-eternity, then it would be valid for Him to be characterized by that contingent attribute in pre-eternity, since receptivity means nothing other than that. But that is impossible, because the contingent cannot be pre-eternal, since it is necessary for the pre-eternal not to accept non-existence, while the contingent has accepted non-existence and is characterized by it, so they are mutually exclusive.
From this it follows for you: that every attribute that the exalted essence accepts is eternal and necessary for it; it is inconceivable that it be contingent. And whatever the exalted essence does not accept in pre-eternity, it never accepts, because of what you know about the impossibility of receptivity occurring to the essence after it did not have it.
Having demonstrated by proof the necessity of pre-eternity and permanence for life and for the attributes that preceded it, which we know by reason and revelation to be attributes of Him, may He be exalted, He intended here to demonstrate by proof the necessity of pre-eternity and permanence for all attributes that subsist in His essence, may He be exalted, in general, whether we know them or do not know them, so that we are certain of the impossibility of the exalted essence being a locus for contingent events, and that it is characterized only by an attribute necessarily pre-eternal and permanent.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage is a general proof that all attributes of God are pre-eternal (qadim) and permanent (baqi). It begins by stating that all 'attributes of meaning' (sifat al-ma'ani) are characterized by pre-eternity and permanence. Then it extends this to all other attributes that subsist in the divine essence. The proof proceeds by reductio: if an attribute were to accept non-existence, it would be contingent (hadith). But the pre-eternal cannot accept non-existence. It is impossible for God to have a contingent attribute; otherwise, His essence would have to be receptive to that attribute in pre-eternity (since receptivity is essential, not acquired). If that receptivity itself were contingent, it would require another receptivity, leading to infinite regress. Therefore, the essence's receptivity to any attribute must be pre-eternal. But if the essence is receptive in pre-eternity, then the attribute would have to be present in pre-eternity, making it pre-eternal, which contradicts its supposed contingency. Hence, all attributes that the essence accepts are eternal. Moreover, whatever the essence does not accept in pre-eternity can never be accepted later, because receptivity cannot arise anew in the essence. The author concludes by clarifying that the purpose is to prove that the divine essence cannot be a locus for temporal events (mahall li'l-hawadith) and that it only has attributes that are necessarily pre-eternal and permanent. This is a foundational argument in Sunni kalam against the possibility of new attributes arising in God.

Misconception: That God could acquire new attributes over time.
Correction: The proof shows that receptivity is essential and cannot arise, so no attribute can be acquired later.

Checkpoint

B) The attribute would still be eternal.
C) The essence would change.
D) It would be acceptable.

Key Takeaway
All of God's attributes are pre-eternal and permanent because the essence cannot be a locus for temporal events.

The proof shows that God cannot acquire new attributes. How does this challenge your concept of God's mercy or anger being 'new'? How should you respond to the fact that God's attributes are always perfectly present?
?
Consider one area where you doubt God's care for you. Does this lesson remind you that God's attributes are not temporary? How should you adjust your reliance on Him?

Proving All Divine Attributes Are Eternal
Sanusi states the goal of proving the eternity of all divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Sanusi aims to prove the eternity and perpetuity of every attribute that subsists in God's essence, and that this is a necessary conclusion from rational demonstration.

Core Idea
Every divine attribute is necessarily eternal, not just some.

Sanusi has already demonstrated the eternity of life and certain prior attributes. Now he extends that proof to all attributes that belong to God, whether known to us through reason or revelation or not. The goal is to establish that God's essence can never be a subject of temporal change, and that every single one of His attributes is necessarily eternal and perpetual.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage slowly
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Note the transition from previous proofs to a broader claim.
The phrase 'لما بيَّن' indicates a transition from what was previously established.
2
Identify the key claim
Find the statement that Sanusi intends to prove: the necessity of eternity and perpetuity for all attributes that subsist in God's essence.
The words 'وجوب القدم والبقاء لسائر الصفات' express this.
3
Understand the scope
Notice that the proof covers attributes 'ما عرفناه منها وما لم نعرفه' (those we know and those we do not). This is a comprehensive claim.
This shows that the proof is not limited to attributes revealed in scripture.
4
Grasp the ultimate conclusion
Sanusi concludes that we must be certain that God's essence cannot be a locus for temporal occurrences, and that all His attributes are necessarily eternal.
The word 'نقطع' emphasizes the certainty required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لما بيَّن بالبرهان وجوب القدم والبقاء للحياة ولما قبلها من الصفات التي عرفنا بالعقل وبالشرع اتصافه تعالى بها .. أراد أن يبين هنا بالبرهان وجوب القدم والبقاء لسائر الصفات التي تقوم بذاته تعالى عموماً ، ما عرفناه منها وما لم نعرفه ، بحيث نقطع باستحالة أن تكون الذات العليَّة محلاً للحوادث ، وأنها لا تتصف إلا بصفة واجبة القدم والبقاء .
When he had proven by demonstration the necessity of eternity and perpetuity for life and for what precedes it of the attributes which we know by reason and by revelation that He, exalted, is described with, he intended to demonstrate here by demonstration the necessity of eternity and perpetuity for the rest of the attributes that subsist in His essence, exalted, generally, those we know of them and those we do not know, such that we are certain of the impossibility that the supreme essence be a locus for temporal occurrences, and that it is not described except with an attribute necessary of eternity and perpetuity.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a transitional statement connecting previous proofs about specific attributes (life and prior attributes) to a general proof for all attributes. Sanusi explains that after establishing the eternalness of those attributes, he now aims to extend that proof to all attributes that subsist in God's essence, whether known to us or unknown. The key point is that we must be absolutely certain that God cannot be the subject of temporal change, and that every attribute He has is necessarily eternal and perpetual. The phrase 'بحيث نقطع' emphasizes the certainty required: this is not a probable conclusion but a demonstrated truth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Correction: Sanusi clarifies here that the proof applies to all attributes, not just a select few.

Divine Attributes

4 min
First proof that all attributes are eternal: impossibility of temporal acceptance
Sanusi presents the first of three proofs that God cannot acquire temporal attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of Sanusi's first proof that God cannot acquire temporal attributes, specifically the argument that acceptance of attributes must be essential to the essence, and the contradiction that would arise from temporal acceptance.

Core Idea
God's essence cannot 'learn' to accept attributes—acceptance must be timeless.

This passage presents the first of three proofs demonstrating that all of God's attributes are eternal and that He cannot be subject to temporal change. Sanusi uses a conditional argument: if a temporal attribute were possible, the essence would need an inherent capacity to accept it in eternity. But that capacity cannot arise later; it must be essential. This leads to an infinite regress if it were temporal. Follow along as we unpack the careful reasoning that leads to the conclusion that no attribute of God can be temporal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the conditional structure.
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Sanusi opens with a conditional: 'if it were permissible that He be described with a temporal attribute...' (لو جاز). This sets up a proof by contradiction.
The proof does not directly state the conclusion; it shows that the assumption leads to an impossibility.
2
Understand the explanation of the implication (بيان الملازمة) and the infinite regress argument.
The next section explains why acceptance (قبول) must be essential (نفسي). If acceptance could arise later, it would need another acceptance, leading to an infinite regress (تسلسل). This shows acceptance is inherent.
The infinite regress is a common argument in kalam: any temporal quality would require a chain of prior acceptances, which is impossible.
3
Grasp the final contradiction: the attribute would have to be both temporal and eternal.
Sanusi then applies this to God: if a temporal attribute were possible, the essence would accept it in eternity, making it eternal. But by assumption it is temporal, so a contradiction arises. Hence, the assumption is false.
This reinforces the distinction between the eternal (necessary, never non-existent) and temporal (preceded by non-existence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ ثلاثة براهين على قدم وبقاء صفاتِ المعاني واستحالة قيام الحوادثِ به تعالى ] واستدل على هذا المطلب بثلاثة براهين : الأوّل : أَنَّهُ لو جاز أن يتَّصف تعالى بصفة حادثة .. للزم أن تكونَ ذاتُهُ العليَّةُ قابلة للاتِّصافِ بتلك الصفة الحادثة في الأزل . وبيان الملازمة في ذلك : أنَّ قبول الذات من حيث هي ذات لكل ما تتَّصف به .. نفسي لها ، لا يمكن أن يطرأ عليها بعد أن لم يكن لها ، إذ لو طرأ عليها قبول الصفة بعد أن لم يكن لها .. لزم ألا تتَّصف بذلك القبول الطارئ حتى يطرأ عليها أيضاً قبول لذلك القبول ، ثم يلزم مثل ذلك في قبول ذلك القبول ، ويلزم التسلسل محال ، فتعيَّن أنَّ قبول كل ذات لما تنعت به لا يكون إلا نفسياً لها ، ويستحيل أن يكون طارئاً عليها بعد أن لم يكن لها . فقد عرفت بهذا الدليل : أنَّ الذات العليَّة لو أمكن أن تتَّصف بصفة حادثة .. لوجب أن تكون قابلة لها في الأزل ، ويلزم من قبولها تلك الصفة الحادثة في الأزل ؛ إذ لا معنى لقبولها صحة وجود الذات لها في الأزل إلا صحة اتصافها بها فيه ، وذلك يستلزم أن يكون الحدوث والقدم جائزين على تلك الصفة ، وذلك مستحيل ؛ إذ القديم من لازمه : أن يكون واجباً، لا يقبل العدم أصلاً ، لا سابقاً ولا لاحقاً ، ومن لازم الحادث : وجوب سبق العدم وجواز لحوقه .
[Three proofs for the eternity and perpetuity of the attributes of meanings and the impossibility of the occurrence of temporal events in Him, exalted.] And he argued for this claim with three proofs: The first: that if it were permissible that He, exalted, be described with a temporal attribute, then it would be necessary that His supreme essence be receptive to being described with that temporal attribute in eternity. And the explanation of the implication in that: that the acceptance of the essence, insofar as it is essence, for everything it is described with, is essential to it, not possible that it should occur to it after not being for it. For if acceptance of the attribute occurred to it after not being for it, then it would be necessary that it not be described with that occurring acceptance until there also occurs to it an acceptance for that acceptance, then the like is required for the acceptance of that acceptance, and an infinite regress would be necessary, which is impossible; thus it is determined that the acceptance of every essence for what it is described with is only essential to it, and it is impossible that it be occurring to it after not being for it. So you have come to know by this proof: that if the supreme essence could possibly be described with a temporal attribute, then it would be necessary that it be receptive to it in eternity, and it would be necessary from its acceptance of that temporal attribute in eternity; since there is no meaning of its acceptance [except] the validity of the existence of the essence having it in eternity except the validity of its being described with it therein, and that necessitates that temporality and eternity be both possible for that attribute, and that is impossible; because from the eternal is necessarily that it be necessary, not accepting non-existence at all, not before nor after, and from the temporal is necessarily the necessity of precedence of non-existence and the permissibility of its subsequent occurrence.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is the first of three proofs that God's attributes are eternal and that He cannot be subject to temporal change. Sanusi presents the argument in two parts: first, establishing that the essence's acceptance of any attribute is essential and cannot arise later (otherwise infinite regress), and second, showing that if a temporal attribute were possible, the essence would have to accept it in eternity, which would make that attribute both temporal and eternal (impossible). The proof begins with a conditional: if God could have a temporal attribute, then He must have the capacity to accept that attribute in eternity. The explanation of the implication (بيان الملازمة) shows that the capacity to accept is essential (نفسي) to the essence—it cannot come into being after not existing. If it could, then that capacity would itself need a capacity to accept it, leading to an endless chain. Therefore, the capacity to accept any attribute must be eternal. So, if a temporal attribute were possible, the essence would have been capable of accepting it in eternity. But accepting it in eternity would mean the attribute exists in eternity, making it eternal. Thus the same attribute would have to be both temporal (by assumption) and eternal (by implication), which is a contradiction. The conclusion is that the very notion of a temporal attribute in God is impossible. Sanusi then reinforces this by contrasting the necessary properties of the eternal (necessity, non-acceptance of non-existence) and the temporal (preceded by non-existence, possible to cease).

Key Terms
صفة حادثة
قبول
نفسي
تسلسل
القدم
الحدوث
واجب
جائز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's acceptance of an attribute could occur in time, as a new capacity arises.
Correction: Sanusi shows that acceptance is essential (نفسي) to the essence and cannot arise later, otherwise an infinite regress follows. Therefore, any attribute God has must be eternal.

Checkpoint
What does Sanusi argue would happen if acceptance of an attribute could occur to God's essence after not being for it?
A) That acceptance would itself need another acceptance, leading to an infinite regress.
B) The attribute would be impossible to receive.
C) The essence would change its nature.
D) The attribute would become necessary.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's first proof demonstrates that God's essence has an essential capacity for attributes, and therefore any attribute must be eternal; attributing a temporal attribute to God leads to logical absurdity.

Since God does not 'learn' to accept you (His acceptance is essential and eternal), what does that imply about your relationship with Him—is it based on His unchanging nature or your fluctuating actions? Which one do you rely on more?
?
The proof shows that a temporal attribute in God is impossible. Are there areas in your life where you subconsciously expect God to 'change' or 'acquire' new qualities to meet your immediate needs? How does this lesson demand a shift in how you perceive and approach God in worship?

Divine Attributes
advanced
8 min
First Proof: Impossibility of Temporal Attributes on Allah
Sanusi presents the first proof against temporal attributes on Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first proof that temporal attributes cannot be ascribed to Allah, including the concepts of essential acceptance and the impossibility of infinite regress.

Core Idea
A temporal attribute cannot be added to Allah without collapsing the distinction between eternal and temporal.

Sanusi begins his set of three proofs by presenting a sophisticated argument that any temporal attribute would require Allah's essence to be receptive to it in pre-eternity—a logical impossibility. This proof establishes that every attribute Allah has must be eternally necessary, not temporally acquired. Let's walk through the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own argument come through.
This proof is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the assumption and its consequence
The proof begins with an assumption: if Allah could have a temporal attribute. What follows?
The consequence is that the essence must be receptive in pre-eternity.
3
Understand essential acceptance and the regress argument
Sanusi argues that acceptance of an attribute is essential, not acquired. If it were acquired, infinite regress would occur. Grasp why this is impossible.
Focus on the concept of 'qabūl nafsī'.
4
Grasp the contradiction between pre-eternity and temporality
Accepting a temporal attribute in pre-eternity makes it both eternal and temporal, a contradiction. Then conclude that no temporal attribute is accepted.
The contrapositive: every accepted attribute is pre-eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثلاثة براهين على قدم وبقاء صفاتِ المعاني واستحالة قيام الحوادثِ بهِ تعالى. واستدل على هذا المطلب بثلاثة براهين: الأوّلُ : أَنَّهُ لو جازَ أنْ يتّصف تعالى بصفة حادثة .. للزم أن تكونَ ذاتُهُ العليَّةُ قابلة للاتّصافِ بتلك الصفة الحادثة في الأزلِ . وبَيانُ الملازمة في ذلكَ : أنَّ قبول الذاتِ مِنْ حيثُ هي ذات لكلِّ ما تتَصفُ بهِ .. نفسي لها ، لا يمكن أن يطرأ عليها بعدَ أنْ لم يكن لها ، إذ لو طراً عليها قبولُ الصفةِ بعد أن لم يكن لها .. لزم ألا تَتَّصفَ بذلك القبولِ الطارئ حتى يطراً عليها أيضاً قبول لذلك القبولِ ، ثم يلزمُ مثلُ ذلكَ في قبولِ ذلك القبولِ ، ويلزم التسلسل محال ، وهو فتعيَّنَ أنَّ قبول كلِّ ذات لما تنصفُ به لا يكون إلا نفسياً لها ، ويستحيل أن يكون طارئاً عليها بعد أن لم يكن لها. فقد عرفت بهذا الدليل : أنَّ الذات العليَّةَ لو أمكن أنْ تتَّصفَ بصفة حادثة . . لوجب أن تكون قابلة لها في الأزلِ ، ويلزمُ مِنْ قبولها تلك الصفة الحادثة في الأزلِ ؛ إذْ لا معنى لقبولِ لها صحَّةُ وجودِ الذاتِ لها في الأزلِ إلا صحَّةُ اتّصافِها بها فيهِ ، وذلك يستلزم أنْ يكونَ الحدوث والقدم جائزين على تلك الصفة ، وذلك مستحيل ؛ إذ القديم مِنْ لازمهِ : أنْ يكونَ واجباً، لا يقبل العدم أصلاً ، لا سـابقـاً ولا لاحقاً ، ومِنْ لازم الحادثِ : وجوبُ سَبْقِ العدمِ وجوازُ لحوقِهِ ، فهما متنافيان بحسَب الموصوفِ بهما ، فما قبل الاتصاف بأحدهما لا يقبلُ الاتصاف بالآخرِ. فإذاً ؛ هذهِ الصفةُ المفروضةُ الحدوثِ لا تقبلها الذات العليَّةُ في الأزلِ ؛ لاستحالةِ أنْ يَتَّصفَ بالقدم كلُّ ما جازَ عليه الحدوث ، وإذا لم تقبلها الذاتُ العليَّةُ في الأزلِ.. لزم ألا تقبلها أبداً ؛ لِمَا عرفْتَ مِن استحالةِ أنْ يطراً على الذاتِ قبولُ الصفةِ بعدَ أنْ لم يكن لها . وإذا لزم ألا تقبل الذاتُ العليَّةُ الصفة الحادثة أبداً . . لزم ألا تتصفَ بها أبداً ؛ لاستحالة اتصاف ذاتِ بصفة وهي لا تقبلها. وخرج لكَ بهذا : أنَّ كلَّ ما قبلَتْهُ الذات العليَّةُ مِنَ الصفاتِ فهو أزلي واجبٌ لها ، وينعكس بعكس النقيض الموافق : إلى أنَّ كلَّ ما ليس بأزلي فلا تقبلُهُ الذاتُ العليَّةُ
Three proofs for the pre-eternity and perpetuity of the attributes of meanings and the impossibility of temporal events occurring to Him, exalted is He. And he argued for this claim with three proofs: The first: that if it were permissible for the Exalted to be described with a temporal attribute... it would necessitate that His exalted essence be receptive to being described with that temporal attribute in pre-eternity. And the explanation of the entailment in that: that the acceptance of the essence, insofar as it is an essence, for everything it is described with... is essential (nafsī) to it, it cannot occur to it after it did not have it, for if acceptance of the attribute occurred to it after it did not have it... it would necessitate that it not be described with that occurring acceptance until another acceptance for that acceptance also occurs to it, then the like of that follows in the acceptance of that acceptance, and infinite regress (tasalsul) would follow, which is impossible. Thus it is determined that the acceptance of every essence for what it is described with is only essential to it, and it is impossible for it to be occurring to it after it did not have it. So you have known by this proof: that if the exalted essence could be described with a temporal attribute... it would be necessary for it to be receptive to it in pre-eternity, and it follows from its acceptance of that temporal attribute in pre-eternity—for there is no meaning of its acceptance of the correctness of the existence of the essence for it in pre-eternity except the correctness of its being described with it therein—and that necessitates that temporality and pre-eternity be both possible for that attribute, and that is impossible; since from the necessary concomitants of the pre-eternal is that it be necessary, not accepting non-existence at all, neither before nor after, and from the necessary concomitants of the temporal is the necessity of precedence of non-existence and the possibility of its subsequent occurrence, so they are mutually exclusive in terms of the described subject, so whatever accepts description by one of them does not accept description by the other. Therefore, this supposed temporal attribute—the exalted essence does not accept it in pre-eternity, because it is impossible for everything upon which temporality is possible to be described with pre-eternity. And if the exalted essence does not accept it in pre-eternity... it follows that it never accepts it, because you know of the impossibility of acceptance of the attribute occurring to the essence after it did not have it. And if it follows that the exalted essence never accepts the temporal attribute... it follows that it is never described with it, because it is impossible for an essence to be described with an attribute while it does not accept it. And it follows from this: that every attribute that the exalted essence accepts is pre-eternal and necessary for it, and it reflects by contrapositive correspondence to: that everything not pre-eternal, the exalted essence does not accept it.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage contains the first of three proofs for the pre-eternity and perpetuity of Allah's attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī) and the impossibility of temporal attributes (ḥawādith) occurring to Him. The proof is structured as a reductio ad absurdum. The argument proceeds as follows: 1. Assume that Allah could be described with a temporal attribute. 2. This would require that His essence be receptive (qābil) to that attribute in pre-eternity (al-azal). 3. Sanusi argues that the essence's receptivity to any attribute it is described with is essential (nafsī) to it, not something that can occur later. If receptivity could occur later, that would require an infinite regress of acceptances, which is impossible. Therefore, receptivity must be essential. 4. If the essence receives the temporal attribute in pre-eternity, then that attribute would be present in pre-eternity, meaning it is both pre-eternal and temporal—a contradiction because pre-eternal entails necessity and impossibility of non-existence, while temporal entails preceding non-existence and possibility of ceasing. 5. Hence the essence cannot accept it in pre-eternity. And if it cannot accept it then, it can never accept it (since receptivity cannot arise anew), so it can never be described with it. 6. The conclusion: every attribute that Allah accepts is pre-eternal and necessary; the contrapositive: everything not pre-eternal is not accepted by Allah.

Key Terms

نفسي
طارئ
تسلسل
قدم
حدوث
صفات المعاني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think an attribute can be added to Allah later, implying He changes or acquires new attributes.
Correction: This proof shows that accepting a temporal attribute would require a contradiction between pre-eternity and temporality, and the essence's acceptance of attributes is essential, not acquired.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, why is it impossible for Allah to be described with a temporal attribute?
A) Because temporal attributes are inherently impure.
B) Because it would require infinite regress of acceptances and lead to contradiction between pre-eternity and temporality.
C) Because Allah's essence cannot accept any attributes at all.
D) Because temporal attributes only apply to created beings, not to the Creator.

Key Takeaway
The first proof demonstrates that Allah cannot accept any temporal attribute because that would require a contradiction between pre-eternity and temporality, and because acceptance of attributes is essential, not accidental.

Objection to the First Proof and Its Answer
Sanusi presents an objection regarding the temporal attributes of humans and gives the beginning of the answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that a fetus's delayed acquisition of attributes raises against the first proof of God's attributes, and the beginning of the refutation.

Core Idea
Acceptance of an attribute does not automatically mean immediate description.

This passage presents a challenge to the earlier proof that if an essence is receptive to an attribute, that attribute must exist immediately. The objector uses the example of a human fetus, which is receptive to knowledge but only acquires it later. Sanusi begins his reply, though the text is cut short. Let's examine the objection and the initial response.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objection carefully from the Arabic and translation. Notice how the objector states the implication they see in your argument.
The objector says your reasoning forces immediate accompaniment of attribute to essence.
2
Understand the example
The objector gives the example of a fetus (al-ḥirm) that is receptive to knowledge and opinion from the start but does not possess them until later, or never. This is used to show that readiness does not guarantee immediate description.
3
See the conclusion
The objector concludes that acceptance of an attribute does not lead to being described with it, let alone the attribute being necessary. This would undermine the first proof if true.
4
Begin the answer
Sanusi begins his reply: 'What we have mentioned only implies that every receptacle for an attribute must necessarily be correct...' The text cuts off, but we can anticipate that the answer distinguishes between temporal and eternal receptacles.
The full answer would likely show that delay is possible for temporal beings but not for the eternal essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : ما ذكرتُموهُ يقتضي أنَّ كلَّ قابل لصفةٍ ما ، سواء كانَ ذلكَ القابلُ قديماً أو حادثاً .. يلزم أن يكون وجود تلك الصفة المقبولة مصاحباً لوجودِهِ لا يتأخَّرُ عنه ، وذلكَ باطل ؛ بدليل أنَّ الحِرْمَ قابل في أوَّلِ أزمنة وجودِهِ لصفاتٍ عديدةٍ ؛ كالعلم والظن ونحوهما ، ثم لا يتّصفُ بها إلا بعد أزمنةٍ مِنْ وجودِهِ ، بل قد لا يتصف بها أصلاً ، فإذاً لا يلزمُ مِنْ قبولِ الذاتِ لصفةٍ ما اتّصافُها بها ، فضلاً عن أنْ تجبَ تلك الصفة لها. قلتُ : الذي ذكرناهُ إِنَّما يقتضي أنَّ كلَّ قابل لصفةٍ فلا بدَّ أنْ يصح
For if you say: What you have mentioned implies that every receptacle for an attribute, whether that receptacle is pre-eternal or temporal... necessitates that the existence of that accepted attribute accompany its existence, not delayed from it, and that is false; by the evidence that a fetus is receptive in the first moments of its existence to many attributes, such as knowledge, opinion, and the like, yet it is not described with them except after periods of its existence, and it may not be described with them at all. Therefore, from the essence's acceptance of an attribute, its being described with it does not follow, let alone that the attribute be necessary for it. I said: What we have mentioned only implies that every receptacle for an attribute must necessarily be correct...
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to the first proof and the beginning of its answer. The objector says: Your reasoning implies that if something is receptive to an attribute, that attribute must exist alongside it immediately. But this is false, because a fetus (al-ḥirm) is receptive to attributes like knowledge and opinion from the start, but only manifests them later, or not at all. So acceptance does not entail immediate description, let alone necessity. The answer begins: 'What we mentioned only implies that every receptacle for an attribute must necessarily be correct...' but the text cuts off. The intended refutation likely explains that the earlier proof applies specifically to the pre-eternal essence, where no delay is possible because temporal delay would imply change in the eternal. The answer is incomplete, so we note the objection and the opening of the reply.

Divine Attributes
beginner
5 min
Proof That Divine Attributes Are Eternal and Necessary
Sanusi proves that divine attributes accepted by the essence are eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that any attribute accepted by the eternal divine essence must be eternal and necessary, and that a temporal attribute can never be accepted.

Core Idea
Divine attributes are eternal because the essence's acceptance is essential and cannot begin.

Sanusi presents a tight logical argument to demonstrate that every attribute truly predicated of Allah must be eternal. The proof hinges on the nature of acceptance (qabūl) as an essential property of the essence, which cannot arise later. Understanding this proof is foundational for the Islamic doctrine of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the logical flow from mutual exclusivity to the conclusion.
The argument uses a conditional chain; pay attention to 'if...then' structures.
2
Identify the key premise
Find the statement that two contradictory attributes (like eternal and temporal) are mutually exclusive for the same subject. This is the starting point.
Mutual exclusivity means they cannot both describe the same thing at the same time.
3
Follow the conditional reasoning
Trace the logical steps: if a temporal attribute is assumed, then the essence does not accept it in eternity; if not accepted in eternity, then never accepted; if never accepted, then never described by it. Observe how each step builds on the previous.
The impossibility of ṭuru' al-qabūl (acceptance arising later) is crucial.
4
Understand the conclusion and contrapositive
The conclusion states that every attribute accepted by the essence is eternal and necessary. Reflect on the contrapositive: whatever is not eternal is not accepted. See how this follows logically.
This proof establishes that divine attributes must be eternal, not acquired in time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهما متنافيان بحسب الموصوف بهما ، فما قبل الاتصاف بأحدهما لا يقبل الاتصاف بالآخر. فإذاً هذه الصفة المفروضة الحدوث لا تقبلها الذات العليَّة في الأزل؛ لاستحالة أن يتَّصف بالقدم كل ما جاز عليه الحدوث، وإذا لم تقبلها الذات العليَّة في الأزل.. لزم ألا تقبلها أبداً؛ لما عرفت من استحالة أن يطرأ على الذات قبول الصفة بعد أن لم يكن لها. وإذا لزم ألا تقبل الذات العليَّة الصفة الحادثة أبداً.. لزم ألا تتصف بها أبداً؛ لاستحالة اتصاف ذات بصفة وهي لا تقبلها. وخرج لك بهذا: أن كل ما قبلته الذات العليَّة من الصفات فهو أزلي واجب لها، وينعكس بعكس النقيض الموافق: إلى أن كل ما ليس بأزلي فلا تقبله الذات العليَّة.
The two are mutually exclusive according to the subject described; whatever precedes being described by one of them does not accept being described by the other. Therefore, this supposed contingent attribute is not accepted by the Most High Essence in eternity, because it is impossible for everything upon which temporality is possible to be described with eternity. And if the Most High Essence does not accept it in eternity, it follows that it will never accept it, because you have known the impossibility of the Essence's acceptance of an attribute occurring later after it was not (so). And if it follows that the Most High Essence never accepts the temporal attribute, it follows that it is never described with it, because it is impossible for an essence to be described with an attribute which it does not accept. And from this it is deduced for you: that every attribute that the Most High Essence accepts is eternal and necessary for it, and it reflects by contrapositive to: that whatever is not eternal, the Most High Essence does not accept it.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage presents a logical proof regarding divine attributes. The author begins by noting that two contradictory attributes (such as eternity and temporality) are mutually exclusive with respect to the same subject. Therefore, if a certain attribute is assumed to be temporal (ḥādith), the eternal Essence cannot accept it in eternity, because that would require the eternal Essence to be described with something temporal, which is impossible. Furthermore, if the Essence does not accept it in eternity, it will never accept it, because acceptance is an essential (dhātī) property of the Essence and cannot arise later. Consequently, the Essence can never be described with that attribute. The conclusion is a general rule: every attribute that the Most High Essence accepts is eternal and necessary (wājib) for It; conversely, any attribute that is not eternal is not accepted by the Essence. This is a classic kalam argument using the necessity of eternal attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'acceptance' (qabūl) means a passive capacity that can be acquired later.
Correction: In this context, acceptance is an essential property of the divine essence that cannot arise later; if the essence does not accept an attribute in eternity, it will never accept it.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why can the eternal Essence not accept a temporal attribute?
A) Because temporal attributes are inherently evil.
B) Because the Essence is simple and cannot have multiple attributes.
C) Because acceptance in eternity is essential and cannot arise later; thus a temporal attribute, by not being accepted in eternity, can never be accepted.
D) Because the Essence does not need attributes.

Key Takeaway
Every attribute that Allah’s essence accepts must be eternal and necessary, as acceptance is an essential property that cannot be acquired later.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every attribute of Allah is eternal and necessary, then His mercy, justice, and power have never been absent and will never change. When you face a situation where you doubt Allah's mercy, does this truth shake your doubt or does your doubt shake the truth? What specific step will you take today to anchor your trust in His unchanging attributes?
?
The proof shows that acceptance of attributes is an essential property of the divine essence—it cannot arise later. If your own acceptance of truth is not essential to you but comes and goes, what does that say about your need for Allah's guidance? Will you plead with Him tonight to make acceptance of truth a fixed part of your character, not a passing state?

Refuting the Objection: Eternal Acceptance Entails Necessity
Sanusi answers an objection on eternal attributes with a trichotomous proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the objection that divine attributes could be acquired later by distinguishing essential acceptance from temporal acceptance and proving that eternal acceptance entails necessity.

Core Idea
Eternal acceptance of an attribute requires its necessity.

This passage presents a sophisticated objection against the earlier proof that divine attributes are eternal and necessary. The objector uses the example of a fetus to argue that capability does not imply actual possession. Sanusi's response clarifies a crucial distinction: for the eternal Essence, acceptance is essential and cannot arise later, leading to a powerful trichotomous proof that the attribute must be necessary.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the objector's claim: if capability (qābil) of an attribute does not force immediate possession, as seen in a fetus, then the earlier argument fails. Understand the counterexample.
The objector uses 'الحرم' (fetus) as an example.
2
Grasp Sanusi's distinction
Notice how Sanusi distinguishes between essential acceptance (dhātī) for the eternal and acquired acceptance for temporal beings. For the eternal, acceptance cannot arise later.
This distinction blocks the analogy between temporal and eternal.
3
Follow the trichotomous proof
The attribute accepted in eternity must be either necessary, impossible, or contingent. See how Sanusi eliminates impossible and contingent, leaving only necessary. Understand why contingency is ruled out due to need for a particulariser (mukhaṣṣiṣ).
This is a clear example of the three rational judgments (wājib, mustaḥīl, jā'iz) in action.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The attribute must be necessary and eternal. This solidifies the doctrine of eternal attributes. Ask yourself how this argument differs from the temporal case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت: ما ذكرتموه يقتضي أن كل قابل لصفة ما، سواء كان ذلك القابل قديماً أو حادثاً.. يلزم أن يكون وجود تلك الصفة المقبولة مصاحباً لوجوده لا يتأخر عنه، وذلك باطل؛ بدليل أن الحرم قابل في أول أزمنة وجوده لصفات عديدة؛ كالعلم والظن ونحوهما، ثم لا يتصف بها إلا بعد أزمنة من وجوده، بل قد لا يتصف بها أصلاً، فإذاً لا يلزم من قبول الذات لصفة ما اتصافها بها، فضلاً عن أن تجب تلك الصفة لها. قلت: الذي ذكرناه إنما يقتضي أن كل قابل لصفة فلا بد أن يصح اتصافه بها مصاحبة لوجوده؛ لما عرفت أن القبول لا يكون إلا ذاتياً للقابل، لا يمكن أن يطرأ عليه بعد أن لم يكن. ولكن إنما لزم في كل صفة تقبلها الذات العليَّة أن تكون واجبة لها أزلية؛ من جهة أنه لما لزم صحة اتصاف الذات العليَّة بها في الأزل؛ لما عرفت أن القبول لا يمكن طريانه على الذات بعد أن لم يكن.. لزم أن تكون تلك الصفة واجبة؛ إذ كل ما صح قدمه لم يقبل أن يكون حادثاً. وبيان ذلك: أن تلك الصفة التي يقبلها القديم أزلاً لا تخلو: إما أن تكون واجبة الوجود، أو مستحيلة الوجود، أو جائزة الوجود. وكونها مستحيلة الوجود واضح البطلان؛ إذ لو كانت كذلك لما قبل أن يتصف بها القديم، بل ولا غيره. وكذا أيضاً يبطل كونها جائزة الوجود، وإلا لما قبلها القديم في الأزل؛ إذ الجائز لا يكون إلا حادثاً؛ لاحتياجه إلى المخصص، والأزل ينافي الاحتياج إلى المخصص، فإذاً حقيقة الجائز تنافي الأزل قطعاً. وإذا بطل القسمان في هذه الصفة التي قبلتها الذات العليَّة في الأزل.. تعين فيها القسم الثالث؛ وهو أن تكون واجبة الوجود، وهو المطلوب. وبعبارة أخرى: إن كون الصفة تقبل الوجود في الأزل يستلزم كون
For if you say: what you have mentioned requires that every entity capable of receiving some attribute, whether that entity is eternal or temporal, necessarily has the existence of that accepted attribute accompanying its existence, not delayed from it, and that is false; as evidence that the fetus is capable at the first moments of its existence of many attributes, such as knowledge, opinion, and the like, but it is not described with them except after periods of time from its existence, and indeed it may not be described with them at all. Therefore, from the Essence's acceptance of some attribute, its being described with it does not follow, let alone that attribute being necessary for it. I say: what we mentioned only requires that every entity capable of a particular attribute must have the soundness of being described with it accompanying its existence; because you have known that acceptance is only essential to the capable entity, and cannot arise upon it after it was not. But the conclusion that every attribute accepted by the Most High Essence is necessary and eternal for it arises only from the fact that, since the soundness of the Most High Essence being described with it in eternity is required (because you have known that acceptance cannot arise upon the Essence after it was not), it follows that that attribute is necessary; for everything the preexistence of which is sound cannot be temporal. And the explanation of that: that attribute which the eternal entity accepts in eternity is not free from being either necessary of existence, impossible of existence, or contingent of existence. Its being impossible of existence is clearly false; for if it were so, it would not have been capable of being described with it, nor would any other. Likewise, its being contingent of existence is also false; otherwise the eternal entity would not have accepted it in eternity, for the contingent is only temporal, due to its need for a particulariser, and eternity precludes the need for a particulariser; thus the reality of contingency is absolutely incompatible with eternity. And when the two divisions are false regarding this attribute which the Most High Essence accepted in eternity, the third division is determined for it: that it is necessary of existence, which is what was sought. And in other words: that the attribute's acceptance of existence in eternity necessitates its being...
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The objector raises a counterexample: if a subject is capable (qābil) of an attribute, it does not necessarily possess it from the beginning; a fetus is capable of knowledge but acquires it later. So the author's earlier argument that acceptance implies actual possession from the start is false, let alone necessity. The author responds by distinguishing between mere possibility (ṣiḥḥat al-ittiṣāf) and actual acceptance. For temporal beings, only the soundness of being described exists from the beginning, not the actual attribute. For the eternal Essence, however, acceptance is essential (dhātī) and cannot be acquired later; therefore, once acceptance in eternity is established, actual possession in eternity is necessary. The author then provides a detailed proof: the attribute accepted in eternity must be either necessary, impossible, or contingent. Impossible is absurd (no one can be described with it). Contingent is also impossible because contingency requires a particulariser (mukhaṣṣiṣ), and eternity precludes that need. Therefore the attribute must be necessary. This is a crisp trichotomous argument showing that eternal acceptance entails necessity.
