مخصص
أزل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If even temporal beings can acquire attributes later, then the same could apply to God, so the earlier argument for eternal attributes fails.
Correction: Sanusi distinguishes essential acceptance (for the eternal) from acquired acceptance (for temporal). For the eternal Essence, acceptance is essential and cannot arise later, so actual possession from eternity is necessary. The temporal analogy does not apply.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the possibility that an attribute accepted by the eternal Essence in eternity could be contingent?
A) Because contingent attributes are always caused by something else, and the eternal Essence cannot have causes.
B) Because the contingent requires a particulariser to bring it into existence, but eternity precludes any need for a particulariser, so contingency contradicts eternity.
C) Because the contingent is always temporal, and the Essence only accepts eternal attributes.
D) Because the author never considered contingency as a possibility.

Key Takeaway
For the eternal Essence, accepting an attribute in eternity necessarily implies its eternal existence and necessity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In this lesson, Sanusi proves that an attribute accepted by the Eternal Essence in eternity must be necessary. Look at your own life: which attributes define you are essential (part of who you truly are) and which are merely accidental (dependent on circumstances)? Are you willing to let go of those accidental identities if Allah strips them away? What does that reveal about your reliance on Him alone?
?
The objector uses the example of a fetus to argue that capability does not guarantee actuality. Consider your faith: you are capable of deep knowledge, sincere worship, and moral excellence. But are you actually embodying them? What particulariser—what external excuse or internal laziness—is preventing you from actualising what you are capable of? How does the eternal necessity of Allah's attributes shame your inconsistency?
?
The proof eliminates contingency for Allah's attributes because contingency requires a particulariser, and eternity precludes any need. Now think about your own existence: you are contingent through and through, needing Allah's constant particularisation every moment. Does this realization humble you? Do you live as if you are self-sufficient, or do you acknowledge your utter dependence on the Necessary Being? Commit to one concrete action today that reminds you of your contingency.

Divine Attributes
intermediate
6 min
Proof that Divine Attributes Are Necessarily Eternal
Sanusi proves divine attributes must be necessary using the three rational judgments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the foundational proof that any attribute truly predicated of God must be necessary and eternal, not contingent or temporal.

Core Idea
Divine attributes cannot be contingent because contingency contradicts eternity.

Sanusi begins a decisive proof that establishes the eternal nature of divine attributes. Using the three rational categories, he eliminates impossibility and contingency, leaving only necessity. This lesson unpacks the core argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and follow the translation. Notice the logical structure and key terms.
Pay attention to the terms 'واجب', 'مستحيل', 'جائز'.
2
Identify the premise
The passage starts with the premise that acceptance of an attribute is essential to the Self. Understand why this implies that the attribute must accompany the Self's existence eternally.
3
Follow the three-way division
The argument divides possible states of an attribute into necessary, impossible, and contingent. See how impossible is immediately rejected, then contingency is rejected because it requires a specifier, which contradicts eternity.
Contingency implies temporal origination (حدوث).
4
Understand the restatement
Sanusi restates the argument using self-sufficiency from the agent. This reinforces the conclusion that the attribute must be necessary.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is that any attribute accepted by the eternal Self must be necessary and eternal. Ask yourself why this matters for understanding God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اتصافه بها مصاحبةً لوجودِهِ ؛ لما عرفتَ أنَّ القبول لا يكون إلا ذاتياً للقابل ، لا يمكنُ أنْ يطرأ عليهِ بعدَ أنْ لم يكن . لكنَّ إنَّما لزمَ في كلَّ صفةٍ تقبلها الذات العليَّةُ أنْ تكون واجبةً لها أزليَّةً ؛ مِنْ جهةِ أَنَّهُ لمَّا لزمَ صحَّةُ اتّصافِ الذاتِ العليَّةِ بها في الأزلِ ؛ لما عرفت أنَّ القبول لا يمكن طريانه على الذاتِ بعد أنْ لم يكن .. لزمَ أنْ تكونَ تلك الصفةُ واجبةً ؛ إذْ كلُّ ما صح قدمُهُ لم يقبل أنْ يكونَ حادثاً. وبيان ذلكَ : أنَّ تلك الصفة التي يقبلها القديم أزلاً لا تخلو : إمَّا أن تكون واجبة الوجودِ ، أو مستحيلة الوجودِ ، أو جائزة الوجود . وكونها مستحيلة الوجودِ واضحُ البطلان ؛ إذْ لو كانَتْ كذلكَ لَمَا قبل أن يتصف بها القديم ، بل ولا غيره. وكذا أيضاً يبطل كونُها جائزة الوجودِ ، وإلا لما قبلها القديم في الأزلِ ؛ إذ الجائز لا يكون إلا حادثاً ؛ لاحتياجه إلى المخصص ، والأزل ينافي الاحتياج إلى المخصص ، فإذاً حقيقة الجائز تنافي الأزل قطعاً. وإذا بطل القسمانِ في هذه الصفة التي قبلتها الذات العليَّةُ في الأزلِ.. تعيَّنَ فيها القسم الثالثُ ؛ وهو أن تكون واجبة الوجودِ ، وهو المطلوب. وبعبارة أخرى : إِنَّ كونَ الصفة تقبلُ الوجودَ في الأَزلِ يستلزم كونَ تلك الصفة غنيّةٌ في ذاتِها عن الفاعل ؛ إذْ كلُّ ما يحتاجُ في ذاتِهِ إلى الفاعل فلا يقبلُ أنْ يُوجَدَ في الأزلِ ، ولا يكون إلا حادثاً على الضرورة ، وإذا وجبَ لتلك الصفةِ الغنى في ذاتِها عن الفاعل .. لزمَ أن تكون واجبة الوجودِ ، وهو المطلوب. وبالجملة : فتأخُرُ الصفة عن الأزلِ يستلزم إمكانها ، وكلُّ ممكن فهو واجب الحدوثِ ، وما وجبَ حدوثه فلا يقبلُ الوجود في الأزلِ ، فإذا الجمع بين كونِ الصفةِ تقبلُها الذاتُ العليَّةُ في الأزلِ ، وبين كونِ تلكَ الصفةِ تقبلُ التأخُرَ عنِ الأَزلِ . . متناقض بلا شكٍّ. فقد ظهر لك بهذا البرهان القاطع ما ذكرناه : أَنَّ كلَّ ما قبلَتْهُ الذات العليَّةُ مِنَ الصفاتِ يلزمُ أنْ يكونَ أزليّاً واجباً لها ، فلا يقبلُ التأخُرَ عن وجودها. وأما ما تقبله الذواتُ الحادثةُ مِنَ الصفاتِ : Its being described with it accompanying its existence; because you know that acceptance is only essential to the acceptor, it cannot occur to it after it was not. But rather it is necessary that every attribute which the supreme Self accepts must be necessary for It and eternal; from the aspect that when the correctness of the supreme Self's being described with it in eternity is necessary—because you know that acceptance cannot occur to the Self after it was not—then that attribute must be necessary; for everything whose eternity is correct cannot be temporal. And the explanation of that: that attribute which the eternal accepts eternally is not free from: either it is necessary of existence, or impossible of existence, or contingent of existence. Its being impossible of existence is clearly false; for if it were so, the eternal would not accept to be described with it, nor indeed any other. Likewise also its being contingent of existence is false; otherwise the eternal would not accept it in eternity; for the contingent is only temporal, due to its need for the specifier, and eternity precludes need for the specifier. So the reality of the contingent contradicts eternity absolutely. And when the two divisions are false for this attribute which the supreme Self accepted in eternity, then the third division is determined for it, which is that it is necessary of existence, and that is the desired. And in other words: the fact that the attribute accepts existence in eternity necessitates that that attribute is self-sufficient in its essence from the agent; for everything that needs in its essence the agent cannot be brought into existence in eternity, and is only temporal necessarily. And when self-sufficiency from the agent is necessary for that attribute, then it must be necessary of existence, and that is the desired. And in summary: the delay of the attribute from eternity entails its contingency, and every contingent is necessarily temporal, and whatever is necessarily temporal cannot accept existence in eternity. So the combination between the fact that the supreme Self accepts the attribute in eternity and the fact that that attribute accepts delay from eternity is a contradiction without doubt. So it has become clear to you by this decisive proof what we mentioned: that every attribute which the supreme Self accepted must be eternal and necessary for It, so it does not accept delay from Its existence. As for the attributes which temporal beings accept: the necessity of them for those beings is not entailed; from the aspect that when those beings are temporal, the delay of what they accept from their existence does not harm the correctness of their being described with it at the time of their existence; for it remains contingent, needing the agent, whether they are described with it at the time of their existence or not. And our Lord, the Free Agent, the Advancer, the Delayer, does what He wills of that, and advances what He wills of that and delays. And in summary: there is no contradiction in the temporal between our saying: it is correct for it to be described with such an attribute at the time of its existence, and our saying: it is correct for that attribute to be delayed from it; for there is no necessary connection between the correctness of the contingent and its occurrence. As for the eternal, our saying: it is correct
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is a proof (برهان) demonstrating that any attribute truly ascribed to God (الذات العليَّة) must be necessary (واجب) and eternal (أزلي), not contingent or temporal. The author begins with a premise: acceptance (قبول) of an attribute by the Self is essential to the Self, not an accidental occurrence. Since the Self is eternal, its acceptance of an attribute must also be eternal. From this, he argues that the attribute itself must be necessary. He then gives a detailed analysis using the three rational judgments (واجب, مستحيل, جائز). The attribute in question cannot be impossible (مستحيل) because that would preclude its being received. It cannot be contingent (جائز) because a contingent attribute requires a specifier (مخصص) that brings it into existence, and contingency implies temporal origination (حدوث), which contradicts eternity (الأزل). Thus it must be necessary (واجب). He then restates the argument: an attribute that exists in eternity must be self-sufficient (غني) without need for an agent, and self-sufficiency entails necessity. He summarizes by noting that if an attribute were to be delayed after eternity, it would be contingent, and every contingent is necessarily temporal, so combining eternity and delay is contradictory. Finally, he contrasts this with temporal beings (ذوات حادثة) where attributes may be contingent and can be delayed; this is because the being itself is temporal and contingent, so there is no contradiction in saying it could receive an attribute later. The proof is complete and decisive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that divine attributes could be contingent and temporal, since God has power to create attributes temporally.
Correction: The proof shows that any attribute truly received by the eternal Self must be necessary and eternal; contingency would require a specifier, which contradicts the nature of eternity.

Checkpoint

A) Because the contingent is impossible to describe the eternal.
B) Because contingency entails a need for a specifier, which contradicts eternity.
C) Because the attribute is self-sufficient by nature.
D) Because the attribute is coeternal with the Self by necessity of logic.

Key Takeaway
Any attribute truly belonging to the eternal Self must be necessary and eternal, not contingent or temporal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Contingency means need for a specifier. You are contingent—every breath you take is an act of God's specification. When was the last time you truly felt your absolute dependence on God in a moment of helplessness? Will you spend five minutes today in silent recognition that you are nothing without Him sustaining you?
?
The passage argues that the eternal cannot accept a temporal attribute. God's attributes are eternal, so He does not 'develop' new qualities over time. Does your relationship with God reflect this unchanging nature? Or do you treat Him as if He had 'good days' and 'bad days' like humans? What would it mean for your worship to be consistent?

The Contradiction of Temporal Attributes for God and the Contrast with Creatures
Sanusi concludes the proof and contrasts divine attributes with created attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why divine attributes cannot be delayed from eternity, and how temporal beings can have contingent attributes without contradiction.

Core Idea
Divine attributes must be eternal; temporal attributes require a specifier, contradicting God's eternity.

Sanusi summarizes his proof by showing the contradiction in delaying divine attributes. He then contrasts this with created beings, where attributes can be contingent and delayed, because the beings themselves are temporal.

Guided Path
1
Read the summary argument
Read the Arabic passage and translation focusing on the summary that delaying an attribute from eternity leads to contradiction.
Notice the use of 'وبالجملة' indicating a summary.
2
Understand the contradiction
If an attribute could be delayed after eternity, it would be contingent, and every contingent is temporal. But eternity precludes temporality, so the attribute must be eternal.
3
Contrast with temporal beings
For created beings, attributes can be delayed because the being itself is temporal. The need for a specifier is not a problem for temporal things.
4
Reflect on God's free agency
Sanusi mentions that God is the free agent who advances or delays attributes as He wills. This underscores that for temporal beings, the timing of attributes is contingent on God's will.
5
Note the incomplete final sentence
The passage ends mid-sentence, but the point is clear: for the eternal, the attribute must accompany existence; for the temporal, it can be delayed.

But rather it is necessary that every attribute which the supreme Self accepts must be necessary for It and eternal; from the aspect that when the correctness of the supreme Self's being described with it in eternity is necessary—because you know that acceptance cannot occur to the Self after it was not—then that attribute must be necessary; for everything whose eternity is correct cannot be temporal. And the explanation of that: that attribute which the eternal accepts eternally is not free from: either it is necessary of existence, or impossible of existence, or contingent of existence. Its being impossible of existence is clearly false; for if it were so, the eternal would not accept to be described with it, nor indeed any other. Likewise also its being contingent of existence is false; otherwise the eternal would not accept it in eternity; for the contingent is only temporal, due to its need for the specifier, and eternity precludes need for the specifier. So the reality of the contingent contradicts eternity absolutely. And when the two divisions are false for this attribute which the supreme Self accepted in eternity, then the third division is determined for it, which is that it is necessary of existence, and that is the desired. And in other words: the fact that the attribute accepts existence in eternity necessitates that that attribute is self-sufficient in its essence from the agent; for everything that needs in its essence the agent cannot be brought into existence in eternity, and is only temporal necessarily. And when self-sufficiency from the agent is necessary for that attribute, then it must be necessary of existence, and that is the desired. And in summary: the delay of the attribute from eternity entails its contingency, and every contingent is necessarily temporal, and whatever is necessarily temporal cannot accept existence in eternity. So the combination between the fact that the supreme Self accepts the attribute in eternity and the fact that that attribute accepts delay from eternity is a contradiction without doubt. So it has become clear to you by this decisive proof what we mentioned: that every attribute which the supreme Self accepted must be eternal and necessary for It, so it does not accept delay from Its existence. As for the attributes which temporal beings accept: the necessity of them for those beings is not entailed; from the aspect that when those beings are temporal, the delay of what they accept from their existence does not harm the correctness of their being described with it at the time of their existence; for it remains contingent, needing the agent, whether they are described with it at the time of their existence or not. And our Lord, the Free Agent, the Advancer, the Delayer, does what He wills of that, and advances what He wills of that and delays. And in summary: there is no contradiction in the temporal between our saying: it is correct for it to be described with such an attribute at the time of its existence, and our saying: it is correct for that attribute to be delayed from it; for there is no necessary connection between the correctness of the contingent and its occurrence. Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is a proof (برهان) demonstrating that any attribute truly ascribed to God (الذات العليَّة) must be necessary (واجب) and eternal (أزلي), not contingent or temporal. The author begins with a premise: acceptance (قبول) of an attribute by the Self is essential to the Self, not an accidental occurrence. Since the Self is eternal, its acceptance of an attribute must also be eternal. From this, he argues that the attribute itself must be necessary. He then gives a detailed analysis using the three rational judgments (واجب, مستحيل, جائز). The attribute in question cannot be impossible (مستحيل) because that would preclude its being received. It cannot be contingent (جائز) because a contingent attribute requires a specifier (مخصص) that brings it into existence, and contingency implies temporal origination (حدوث), which contradicts eternity (الأزل). Thus it must be necessary (واجب). He then restates the argument: an attribute that exists in eternity must be self-sufficient (غني) without need for an agent, and self-sufficiency entails necessity. He summarizes by noting that if an attribute were to be delayed after eternity, it would be contingent, and every contingent is necessarily temporal, so combining eternity and delay is contradictory. Finally, he contrasts this with temporal beings (ذوات حادثة) where attributes may be contingent and can be delayed; this is because the being itself is temporal and contingent, so there is no contradiction in saying it could receive an attribute later. The proof is complete and decisive.

الحادث
الفاعل المختار
المخصص

Misconception: Some might mistakenly think that if God can create attributes temporally for creatures, He could also have temporal attributes.
Correction: The proof shows that for the eternal Self, any attribute must be eternal; temporal attributes are only possible for temporal beings because they themselves are contingent and need a specifier.

Key Takeaway

How must your heart be reoriented if you truly accept that God alone has necessary, eternal attributes?

The Proof That Divine Attributes Are Eternal
Sanusi proves divine attributes must be eternal and necessary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that all divine attributes are eternal and necessary of existence, and how this differs from temporal attributes.

Core Idea
Divine attributes must be eternal; any delay would be a logical contradiction.

Sanusi presents a conclusive proof that every attribute truly subsisting in God's essence must be eternal. He argues that if an attribute needed an agent to bring it into existence, it could not exist in pre-eternity. This leads to the necessity that God's attributes are wajib al-wujud. He then contrasts this with temporal beings, where attributes can be delayed without contradiction. This passage is foundational for understanding God's timeless nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its rhythm. Then read the translation to understand the argument.
The argument moves from a general principle to a specific conclusion.
2
Identify the key premise
Notice the initial statement: the attribute is self-sufficient of the agent (ghaniyy 'an al-fa'il). This is the core premise.
Self-sufficiency here means no external cause needed.
3
Follow the logical steps
Trace how the author deduces that such an attribute must be necessary of existence, and then shows impossibility of delay.
4
Contrast with temporal beings
Observe how the author distinguishes divine attributes from those of created things, where delay is possible.
5
Understand the conclusion
The combination of 'accepted in pre-eternity' and 'able to be delayed' is contradictory – this is the heart of the proof.
This contradiction is called 'inversion of realities' (qalb al-haqa'iq).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

That attribute is self-sufficient of the agent; for everything that needs in its essence the agent cannot accept to exist in pre-eternity, and is only temporal necessarily. And when self-sufficiency of the agent is necessary for that attribute, it follows that it is necessary of existence, which is what is sought. In sum: the delay of the attribute from pre-eternity entails its possibility, and every possible is necessary of occurrence, and what is necessary of occurrence does not accept existence in pre-eternity. So the combination between the attribute being accepted by the exalted essence in pre-eternity and its being able to be delayed from pre-eternity is a contradiction without doubt. Thus it has become clear to you by this conclusive proof what we mentioned: that every attribute that the exalted essence accepts must be pre-eternal and necessary for it, not accepting delay after its existence. As for what temporal essences accept of attributes: their necessity for those essences does not follow, because those essences being temporal, the delay of their accepted attribute after their existence does not invalidate the soundness of their being described with it at the time of its existence; since it remains contingent, needing the agent, whether described at the time of its existence or not. And our Lord, the free agent, the advancer, the delayer, does what He wills of that, and advances what He wills of that and delays. In sum: there is no contradiction in the temporal between our saying: it is sound for it to be described with such an attribute at the time of its existence, and our saying: it is sound for that attribute to be delayed from it; for there is no necessary connection between the soundness of the contingent and its occurrence. As for the eternal, our saying: it is sound for Him to be described with such an attribute in pre-eternity contradicts the soundness of delaying that attribute from pre-eternity; because of the inversion of realities; for the soundness of the existence of the attribute in pre-eternity entails its being necessary, as we have explained previously, and the soundness of its delay from pre-eternity entails its being contingent, as has also been explained previously. So combining them is an unintelligible contradiction and an inversion of reality, by making the necessary contingent and the contingent necessary. So adhere to this investigation in this station; for it is a slipping of feet, and you will not find - Allah knows best - who has removed the veil from the face of this proof as we have removed it. Praise be to Allah Almighty, and from Him is success; there is no lord other than Him.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage presents a proof that all attributes of God must be pre-eternal (azali) and necessary of existence (wajib al-wujud), not temporal (hadith). The author argues as follows: An attribute that is truly subsisting in God's essence must be self-sufficient of any external agent for its existence, because if it needed an agent, it would not be possible for it to exist in pre-eternity (since that would require an agent acting in pre-eternity, which is impossible because pre-eternity is before all action). Therefore, such an attribute is necessary of existence—it exists eternally and cannot be created. The author then contrasts this with temporal things: a temporal essence can acquire an attribute after its existence, because the attribute remains contingent and possible, and its delay does not affect the essence's description at the time of existence. There is no contradiction in the temporal case. But for the eternal God, saying that He is described with an attribute in pre-eternity and yet that attribute could be delayed (i.e., come into existence later) is contradictory: it would require the same attribute to be both necessary (because it exists in pre-eternity) and contingent (because it could be delayed), which is a plain contradiction. The author emphasizes the strength of this proof and claims unique clarity in presenting it.

أزل
واجب الوجود
ممكن
حادث
فاعل
قلب الحقائق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God can acquire new attributes like creatures do.
Correction: This passage shows that would lead to contradiction because God's attributes are intrinsic and eternal; any delay would require contingency, which is incompatible with divine perfection.

Checkpoint
Why does the author assert that a divine attribute must be wajib al-wujud?
A) Because it is possible in itself.
B) Because it is self-sufficient of the agent in its essence.
C) Because it is created in time.
D) Because it can be delayed from pre-eternity.

Key Takeaway
Divine attributes are eternal and necessary, and any delay would be a logical contradiction, unlike temporal attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's attributes are eternal and necessary, unchanging and inseparable from Him, how does that challenge your daily trust in His promises? When you fear He might delay His help, are you effectively imagining that His attribute of mercy could be contingent or subject to change? Will you repent from such thoughts and anchor your reliance on His eternal attributes?
?
The proof shows that any delay in God's attributes would be a logical contradiction. Do you ever act as if God's attributes—like His justice or mercy—are not fully present at every moment? For example, when you sin, do you doubt that His mercy is still with you, as if it could be withheld? How does this lesson demand you correct your perception of God?
?
Sanusi warns that this point is a 'slipping of feet'. Have you ever slipped into thinking that God acquires new attributes or that He might change? When you reflect on your own faith, is there even a subtle doubt that God's attributes might not be exactly as He has described them? Will you now commit to affirming with certainty that every attribute of God is eternal and necessary, without any possibility of delay or change?

Second Proof: God Cannot Acquire Temporal Attributes
Sanusi argues that God cannot acquire a temporal attribute because He would then be devoid of its opposite.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God cannot acquire a temporal attribute based on the principle that He cannot be devoid of attributes.

Core Idea
If God could lack an attribute, He could lack all attributes—impossible.

In this second proof, Sanusi deepens the argument that God's attributes cannot be temporal. He uses a logical chain: if God were to acquire a new attribute, He would have been without it before; but being without an attribute would imply the possibility of being without all attributes, which is impossible for God's essential attributes like knowledge and power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice that the passage cuts off mid-sentence—this is a fragment of a longer proof.
2
Identify the hypothetical condition
The proof begins with 'if the Exalted is described by a temporal attribute'. This is a conditional statement. Follow the logical consequence that follows.
3
Trace the logical chain
If God could be devoid of one temporal attribute, then by the same reasoning He could be devoid of any attribute. This would contradict the impossibility of His being devoid of essential attributes like knowledge and power.
The proof is meant to conclude that all divine attributes are eternal, not temporal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان الثاني: وأيضاً : لوِ اتَّصفَ تعالى بصفةٍ حادثة لم يجز أنْ يَعرى عنها ، أو عن ضدها ، أو عن مثلها ، وإلا لجاز عروه عن جميع الصفاتِ ؛ لأنَّ قبوله لها ذاتي لا يختلف ، وقد عرفْتَ فيما سبق استحالةَ عروِّهِ عن العلم والقدرةِ والإرادة والحياة . فثبت : أَنَّ كلَّ ما يقبلُهُ مِنَ الصفاتِ لا يعرى عنه إلا
The second proof: Also, if the Exalted is described by a temporal attribute, it is not permissible for Him to be devoid of it, or of its opposite, or of its like; otherwise, it would be permissible for Him to be devoid of all attributes, because His acceptance of them is essential and does not differ. And you have known previously the impossibility of His being devoid of knowledge, power, will, and life. So it is established that every attribute that He accepts, He is not devoid of it except...
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage presents a second proof (al-burhān al-thānī) to show that God cannot acquire a temporal attribute. The reasoning: If God were to acquire a temporal attribute at some time, then before that time He would have been devoid of that attribute. But being devoid of an attribute is either permissible or impermissible. If it were permissible for Him to be devoid of this attribute, then by the same token it would be permissible for Him to be devoid of all attributes, because His capacity to accept attributes is essential and does not vary. But we already know it is impossible for God to be devoid of essential attributes like knowledge, power, will, and life. Therefore, it is impossible for God to be devoid of any attribute that He accepts. Hence, He must always have that attribute; it cannot be temporal. The proof is incomplete in the given text, but the intended conclusion is clear: all divine attributes are eternal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God can acquire new attributes over time, such as becoming the creator after creating.
Correction: This proof shows that if God could acquire a temporal attribute, He would have been devoid of it before. But being devoid of any attribute is impossible for God's essential attributes (knowledge, power, etc.), and by extension for any attribute He accepts. Therefore, all divine attributes are eternal.

Checkpoint
What does the author say would be permissible if God could be devoid of a temporal attribute?
A) That God could be devoid of all attributes.
B) That God could have multiple temporal attributes.
C) That God could change His essence.
D) That God could create the universe.

Key Takeaway
God cannot acquire temporal attributes because that would require Him to have been devoid of them, which is impossible for His essential attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The proof shows that God's attributes are necessary and not accidental. Does your worship reflect this certainty? When you pray, do you truly rely on His unchanging will and power? Challenge: before your next prayer, intentionally meditate on one eternal attribute of God and let that anchor your trust.
?
You have learned that God cannot acquire attributes because that would imply deficiency. How does this affect your view of God's actions in history? Are you tempted to think that God's attributes change in response to creation? Repent of any such notion and embrace that His attributes are perfect and timeless.

The Second Proof: The Impossibility of Temporal Attributes in God's Essence
Sanusi presents the second proof against temporal attributes, arguing from the implications of acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second proof (al-burhan al-thani) that God's essence cannot accept temporal attributes, and how it relies on the logical implications of acceptance, opposites, and similars.

Core Idea
A temporal attribute would force God's essence to accept its opposite or similar—both temporal—making the essence itself temporal.

Sanusi now presents the second proof against the possibility of temporal attributes subsisting in God's essence. This argument delves deeper into the logical structure of 'acceptance' (qabul) and shows that if an eternal essence were to accept a temporal attribute, it would be forced to accept its opposites and similars, all of which are temporal, thus entailing the temporality of the essence itself—an impossibility for the Creator. This proof builds on the concept of acceptance as a necessary concomitant.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify its structure
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Notice that it begins with a summary, then explains the principle of acceptance, then applies it to the hypothetical temporal attribute, and finally addresses an objection.
The passage is dense; take your time to follow the logical flow.
2
Understand the key concept: acceptance (qabul)
Sanusi establishes that acceptance is not a psychological attribute but a rational precondition: if an essence accepts one attribute, it must accept all attributes of that kind. This is crucial for the proof.
This universal acceptance is proven by the necessity of the essential attributes (knowledge, power, etc.).
3
Follow the logical chain for temporal attributes
Start from the supposition that God's essence accepts a temporal attribute. Then, because of the nature of temporality (prior and posterior non-existence), the essence must also accept its opposite or similar. Both are temporal, so the essence would be temporal—contradicting its eternity.
The chain relies on the impossibility of the eternal ceasing to exist.
4
Examine the refutation of the objection
An objector might claim the essence accepts only that specific temporal attribute and no other. Sanusi refutes this by showing that even if so, the attribute would be eternal (since the essence never loses it), contradicting its temporality.
This final part is incomplete in the passage, but the gist is clear.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للاتّصافِ بضدّهِ أو مثلِهِ (۱) ، لكنَّ ضدَّ تلك الصفة الحادثة أو مثلَها لا يكون إلا حادثاً ؛ بدليل طريانِ عدمِهِ ؛ إذ القديم لا ينعدم ، وما لا يعرى عن الحوادث يكون حادثاً ضرورةً ، فلزمَ أَنَّهُ لوِ اتَّصفَ تعالى بصفة حادثة لوجب حدوثه ضرورةً ، وقد عرفت وجوبَ قدمِهِ جلَّ وعلا. هذا هو البرهان الثاني على استحالة قيام الحوادث بذاتِهِ تعالى وتقريرُهُ أَنْ يُقالَ : لوِ اتَّصفَ تعالى بصفة حادثة للزم حدوثه ، ذلك علوّاً كبيراً ، وبيانُ اللزومِ في ذلكَ : أَنَّ القبول قد تقرَّرَ تعالى عن أنَّهُ صفةٌ نفسيَّةُ للقابل ، فيلزمُ ألا يختلف ، فإذا ما وجبَ لبعض الصفاتِ التي تقبلها ذات أيُّ ذات كانَتْ يجب لسائرِ تلك الصفاتِ. وقد تقرَّرَ بالبرهان القاطعِ : الوجوبُ لصفات تقبلها ذات مولانا جلَّ وعزَّ ؛ وهي العلم والقدرة والإرادة والحياة ، وأن تجرد الذات العليَّةِ عن هذهِ الصفاتِ مستحيل عقلاً ، فكذا يجب إذا للذات العليَّةِ كلُّ صفةٍ تقبلها ، وعرؤُها عن تلك الصفة مستحيل. فإذا عرفت هذا فنقولُ : لو فُرِضَ اتصافُهُ تعالى بصفةٍ حادثة .. لزمَ أنْ تكونَ ذاتُهُ جَلَّ وعزَّ قابلة لتلك الصفة ، أو لضدها ، أو مثلها. أمَّا لزوم قبولِهِ لتلك الصفةِ : فظاهرُ ؛ لفَرْضِ صِحَّةِ اتّصافِهِ بها تعالى عن ذلك علوّاً كبيراً . وأمَّا لزوم قبولِهِ لضدّها أو مثلها : فلأنَّ تلك الصفةَ لمَّا فُرِضَتْ حادثة كانَ عدمها السابق واجباً ، والعدمُ اللاحق جائزاً ، فعند عدمها السابق أو اللاحقِ إِمَّا أنْ تنعدم الذاتُ معَها إِنْ فُرِضَ أَنَّ الذات لا تقبلُ غيرها ، ولا يخفى حينَئِذٍ لزوم حدوثِ الذاتِ ، أو تبقى الذات بعد عدمِ تلك الصفة ، فلا بدَّ حينَئِذٍ مِنِ اتِّصافِ الذاتِ بضد تلك الصفة أو مثلها ، وإن لم تقبل ضدَّها تعيَّنَ أنْ تقبل مثلها ، وضدُّها ومثلها لا يكونان إلا حادثين ؛ لأنَّهما إِنْ تَأخَّرَ وجودهما عن تلك الصفة الحادثة فحدوثهما ظاهر ، وإن تقدَّمَ عليها فطروء عدمِهما عندَ الاتصافِ بتلك الصفة الحادثة.. يستلزم نفي قدمهما ؛ لما عرفْتَ أَنَّ القديم لا يصح عدمُهُ. وإذا وجب الحدوث لهذهِ الثلاثةِ لزمَ مِنْ قبولِ الذاتِ واحداً منها أن تكونَ حادثة ؛ لوجوب ملازمة الذاتِ حينئذٍ لما تقبله ، وهو أحد هذه الثلاثة الحادثة لا بعينه. ولا يصح ادّعاءُ أَنَّ الذات لا تقبلُ ضدَّ تلك الصفة الحادثة ولا مثلَها ; لأنَّ فَرْضَ قبولِ الذاتِ للاتّصافِ بتلك الصفة الحادثة يستلزم قبولها لمثلها ضرورةً . وأيضاً : فهذه الدعوى تستلزم حدوث الذاتِ ضرورةً ; لأنَّها إذا لم تقبل إلا تلك الصفة الحادثة.. لزمَ ألا تتجرَّد عنها ، وتلك الصفةُ
For being described by its opposite or its similar (1), but the opposite of that temporal attribute or its similar is only temporal; by evidence of the occurrence of its non-existence; for the eternal does not become non-existent, and that which is not free from temporal things is necessarily temporal. So it necessarily follows that if the Most High were described by a temporal attribute, His temporality would necessarily be necessary, and you have known the necessity of His eternal nature, exalted and majestic. This is the second proof of the impossibility of temporal attributes subsisting in His essence, exalted, and its formulation is to say: If the Most High were described by a temporal attribute, His temporality would necessarily follow—that is far exalted above that—and the explanation of the necessitation in that: that acceptance has been established as being high above being a psychological attribute of the acceptor, so it necessarily follows that it does not differ. So if some of the attributes that any essence accepts are necessary, then all of those attributes are necessary. And it has been established by decisive proof: the necessity for attributes accepted by the essence of our Lord, exalted and majestic—and they are knowledge, power, will, and life—and that the essence's being stripped of these attributes is rationally impossible. So likewise every attribute that the essence accepts must be necessary, and its being stripped of that attribute is impossible. So if you understand this, we say: If it is supposed that the Most High is described by a temporal attribute, it would necessarily follow that His essence, exalted and majestic, is accepting of that attribute, or its opposite, or its similar. As for the necessity of its acceptance of that attribute: it is apparent, because of the assumption of the validity of His being described by it—He is far exalted above that. As for the necessity of its acceptance of its opposite or its similar: because when that attribute is assumed temporal, its prior non-existence is necessary, and its posterior non-existence is possible. So at the time of its prior or posterior non-existence, either the essence ceases to exist along with it, if it is assumed that the essence does not accept other than it—and it is not hidden then the necessitation of the temporality of the essence—or the essence remains after the non-existence of that attribute, so then there must be the description of the essence by the opposite of that attribute or its similar. And if it does not accept its opposite, it is determined to accept its similar. And its opposite and its similar are only temporal, because if their existence is posterior to that temporal attribute, their temporality is apparent; and if they are prior to it, then the occurrence of their non-existence upon being described by that temporal attribute necessitates the negation of their eternity, because you know that what is eternal cannot correctly undergo non-existence. And if temporality is necessary for these three, it follows from the essence's acceptance of one of them that it is temporal, because of the necessary concomitant of the essence then with what it accepts, which is one of these three temporal things not specifically determined. And it is not valid to claim that the essence does not accept the opposite of that temporal attribute nor its similar, because the assumption of the essence's acceptance of being described by that temporal attribute necessitates its acceptance of its similar necessarily. Also: this claim necessitates the temporality of the essence necessarily, because if it accepts only that temporal attribute, it would follow that it is not stripped of it—and that attribute...
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is a proof (the second proof) demonstrating that it is impossible for God (the Most High) to be described with temporal (accidental) attributes. The commentary follows the author's argumentative order.

The author begins by stating the overall proof: If God were described by a temporal attribute, then the opposite or similar of that attribute would also be temporal (since only temporal things have opposites or similars that are also temporal; the eternal does not become non-existent). Therefore, if God accepted a temporal attribute, He would necessarily be temporal—contradicting His necessary eternal nature.

Then the author explains the necessitation in more detail. He establishes that 'acceptance' (qabul) is not a psychological attribute of the acceptor; rather, it is a rational precondition. If an essence accepts one attribute, it must accept all attributes of that kind. Since we have decisive proof that God's essence accepts the necessary attributes (knowledge, power, will, life), and these are necessary, then any attribute that the essence accepts must be necessary. Therefore, if we suppose God accepts a temporal attribute, that attribute would be necessary—but that contradicts its temporality. Thus, the supposition is impossible.

The author then breaks down the logical options: if the essence accepts a temporal attribute, it must also accept its opposite or its similar. Why? Because the temporal attribute has a prior non-existence (necessary) and a posterior non-existence (possible). At the time of its non-existence, either the essence ceases (which would make it temporal) or the essence persists. If it persists, it must be described by the opposite or similar of the original attribute. Both the opposite and similar are temporal (since they either follow the original temporal attribute or precede it; if they precede, their non-existence upon the arrival of the original attribute shows they are not eternal, as the eternal cannot cease). So the essence's acceptance of a temporal attribute forces it to accept a temporal opposite or similar, which makes the essence itself temporal (because it is necessarily accompanied by a temporal attribute).

The author then addresses a possible objection: someone might claim the essence accepts only that specific temporal attribute and neither its opposite nor similar. The author refutes this by noting that the very assumption that the essence accepts that attribute implies the possibility of accepting its similar (if not its opposite). Furthermore, if the essence only accepted that one attribute, it would never be free from it, making it eternal—but the attribute itself is temporal, which is a contradiction. Therefore, the claim is invalid.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God could accept a temporal attribute without any consequences, simply because He is all-powerful.
Correction: The proof shows that the logical structure of acceptance and temporality makes it impossible; even omnipotence cannot violate logical necessity, as the essence would then become temporal.

Key Takeaway
The second proof demonstrates that acceptance of any attribute by an essence necessitates acceptance of all attributes of that class, so if God's essence were to accept a temporal attribute, it would be forced to accept temporal opposites/similars, proving His transcendence.

Proof from Alternation of Attributes
Sanusi proves that accepting a temporal attribute entails temporality of the essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's logical proof that accepting a temporal attribute in an essence necessitates that the essence itself is temporal, through the requirement of opposite or similar attributes.

Core Idea
A temporal attribute forces its bearer to be temporal.

This passage presents a logical proof (burhān) that it is impossible for a pre-eternal essence to accept a temporal attribute. Sanusi builds the argument in stages, showing that accepting one temporal attribute requires the essence to also accept its opposite or similar, which must themselves be temporal, and consequently the essence itself must be temporal. He then addresses and refutes a potential objection. This is a foundational argument in Sunni theology for the attributes of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof's opening statement
Read the first few lines where Sanusi states the necessity of accepting the attribute itself. Note the phrase 'it is apparent' — he considers this obvious under the assumption.
2
Trace the argument for opposite and similar
Follow Sanusi's reasoning: at the time of the attribute's non-existence, the essence either perishes or remains. If it remains, it must accept the opposite or similar. Understand why this is necessary.
3
Understand why the opposite and similar are temporal
Sanusi argues that the opposite and similar can only be temporal, whether they come before or after the original attribute. Grasp the reasoning involving their non-existence and pre-eternity.
4
Refute the objection
Sanusi addresses a claim that the essence might accept only that one attribute. He refutes it by showing it entails temporality as well. Finish by reading the concluding prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمَّا لزوم قبولِهِ لتلك الصفةِ : فظاهرُ ؛ لفَرْضِ صِحَّةِ اتّصافِهِ بها تعالى عن ذلك علوّاً كبيراً . وأمَّا لزوم قبولِهِ لضدّها أو مثلها : فلأنَّ تلك الصفةَ لمَّا فُرِضَتْ حادثة كانَ عدمها السابق واجباً ، والعدمُ اللاحق جائزاً ، فعند عدمها السابق أو اللاحقِ إِمَّا أنْ تنعدم الذاتُ معَها إِنْ فُرِضَ أَنَّ الذات لا تقبلُ غيرها ، ولا يخفى حينَئِذٍ لزوم حدوثِ الذاتِ ، أو تبقى الذات بعد عدمِ تلك الصفة ، فلا بدَّ حينَئِذٍ مِنِ اتِّصافِ الذاتِ بضد تلك الصفة أو مثلها ، وإن لم تقبل ضدَّها تعيَّنَ أنْ تقبل مثلها ، وضدُّها ومثلها لا يكونان إلا حادثين ؛ لأنَّهما إِنْ تَأخَّرَ وجودهما عن تلك الصفة الحادثة فحدوثهما ظاهر ، وإن تقدَّمَ عليها فطروء عدمِهما عندَ الاتصافِ بتلك الصفة الحادثة يستلزم نفي قدمهما ؛ لما عرفْتَ أَنَّ القديم لا يصح عدمُهُ . وإذا وجب الحدوث لهذهِ الثلاثةِ لزمَ مِنْ قبولِ الذاتِ واحداً منها أن تكونَ حادثة ؛ لوجوب ملازمة الذاتِ حينئذٍ لما تقبله ، وهو أحد هذه الثلاثة الحادثة لا بعينه . ولا يصح ادّعاءُ أَنَّ الذات لا تقبلُ ضدَّ تلك الصفة الحادثة ولا مثلَها ؛ لأنَّ فَرْضَ قبولِ الذاتِ للاتّصافِ بتلك الصفة الحادثة يستلزم قبولها لمثلها ضرورةً . وأيضاً : فهذه الدعوى تستلزم حدوث الذاتِ ضرورةً ؛ لأنَّها إذا لم تقبل إلا تلك الصفة الحادثة لزمَ ألا تتجرَّد عنها ، وتلك الصفةُ لم تكن في الأزلِ ، فيلزمُ أنْ تكونَ الذاتُ الملازمة لها كذلك ، كما أشرنا إلى هذا المعنى آنفاً ، وبالله تعالى التوفيق
As for the necessity of its accepting that attribute: it is apparent, due to the assumption of the correctness of His being described by it—exalted is He above that, a great exaltation. And as for the necessity of its accepting its opposite or similar: because when that attribute is assumed to be temporal, its prior non-existence is necessary and its subsequent non-existence is possible. So at the time of its prior or subsequent non-existence, either the essence itself ceases to exist along with it, if it is assumed that the essence does not accept anything else—and then the temporality of the essence is obvious—or the essence remains after the non-existence of that attribute, in which case the essence must inevitably be described by the opposite of that attribute or its similar. And if it does not accept its opposite, then it must accept its similar. But its opposite and its similar can only be temporal; because if their existence comes after that temporal attribute, their temporality is apparent, and if it precedes it, then the occurrence of their non-existence at the time of being described by that temporal attribute necessitates negating their pre-eternity, since you know that the pre-eternal cannot cease to exist. And when temporality is necessarily entailed for these three, then from the essence accepting one of them, it follows that it is temporal, due to the necessity of the essence at that time accompanying what it accepts, which is one of these three temporal things, not specifically determined. And it is not valid to claim that the essence does not accept the opposite of that temporal attribute nor its similar; because the assumption of the essence accepting to be described by that temporal attribute necessitates its acceptance of its similar necessarily. Also, this claim necessarily entails the temporality of the essence; because if it does not accept anything except that temporal attribute, then it must not be free from it, and that attribute did not exist in pre-eternity, so the essence accompanying it must also be such, as we indicated this meaning earlier. And with Allah Almighty is success.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a proof (burhān) that it is impossible for temporal attributes (al-ḥawādith) to subsist in the essence of Allah. The author builds the argument sequentially. First, he states that if an essence is assumed to accept a temporal attribute (ṣifa ḥāditha), the necessity of it accepting that specific attribute is apparent because of the assumption itself. Then he argues that the essence must also accept either the opposite (ḍidd) or the similar (mithl) of that attribute. The reasoning: that temporal attribute has prior non-existence (wājib) and possible subsequent non-existence. At the moment of non-existence, either the essence perishes (proving it temporal) or it remains. If it remains, it must take on the opposite or similar. If it does not accept the opposite, it must accept the similar. Both are temporal because if they appear after, they are temporal; if they existed before, their non-existence at the time of the new attribute would negate their pre-eternity (since a pre-eternal cannot cease). Thus all three possibilities (the original attribute, its opposite, its similar) are temporal. Therefore, the essence that accepts any one of them must itself be temporal because it necessarily accompanies that temporal thing. The author then refutes a potential objection: one might claim the essence accepts only that one temporal attribute, neither its opposite nor its similar. This claim is invalid because accepting that one attribute necessitates accepting its similar. Moreover, such a claim would force the essence to be inseparable from that attribute, which was absent in pre-eternity, thus the essence would also be temporal. He concludes with 'And with Allah is success.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God could acquire a new attribute without affecting His eternality.
Correction: This proof shows that accepting any temporal attribute at all would force the essence to be temporal, because it requires the essence to accept a temporal opposite or similar, and the essence necessarily accompanies what it accepts.

Checkpoint
According to the proof, why must an essence that accepts a temporal attribute also accept its opposite or similar?
A) Because the attribute itself demands this by definition.
B) Because at the time of the attribute's non-existence, the essence must either cease or remain; if it remains, it must be described by something opposite or similar.
C) Because opposites cannot coexist in the same subject.
D) Because the attribute is eternal and requires a counterpart.

Key Takeaway
An essence that accepts a temporal attribute must itself be temporal.

This proof shows that any temporal change in Allah's essence is impossible. Does your heart truly rest in that unchangeability, or do you sometimes long for a God who 'responds' as if He were changing? What would it mean for your faith if Allah could acquire new attributes?
?
If you accept that Allah cannot be described by temporal attributes, then what does it mean for you to ask Him for something new? How does this affect your understanding of du'ā' and divine decree? Write down one way you will adjust your perspective on du'ā' to align with this truth.

The Third Proof: Perfection and Deficiency
Sanusi presents the third proof using a dichotomy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third proof that Allah cannot be described by temporal attributes, based on the dichotomy of perfection and deficiency.

Core Idea
Any temporal attribute of God would imply a deficiency, which is impossible.

Sanusi presents a powerful argument that any attribute Allah acquires in time would either be a deficiency or a perfection that was previously absent—both impossible. This proof relies on the consensus that Allah is only described with perfection. Let's explore the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of the argument, then read the literal translation. Notice the logical structure of the proof.
The proof uses a dichotomy: attribute of deficiency or attribute of perfection.
2
Identify the two branches
Find where Sanusi divides the temporal attribute into two possibilities: either an attribute of deficiency (ṣifat naqṣ) or an attribute of perfection (ṣifat kamāl).
3
Understand why each branch is impossible
For the deficiency branch: it directly attributes deficiency to Allah, which is impossible by consensus. For the perfection branch: because the attribute is temporal, it was absent in pre-eternity, implying a lack of perfection—which is also a deficiency.
This step shows the entailment (mulāzama) clearly.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Since both options lead to impossibility, the assumption that Allah can be described by a temporal attribute is false. Therefore, Allah cannot have temporal attributes.
The proof is a classic reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ البرهان الثالث ] وأيضاً : فهو جلَّ وعزَّ لا يتّصفُ إلا بالكمال إجماعاً فيلزمُ في هذه الصفة الحادثة التي فُرِضَ اتصافُهُ تعالى بها أن تكونَ مِنْ صفاتِ الكمال ، وقد فاتَتْ ذاته العليَّةَ في الأزل ؛ لفَرْضِ حدوثها ، وفوتُ الكمال نقص ، وهو تعالى مُنزَّه عنه بإجماع العقلاء . هذا هو البرهان الثالثُ على استحالة قيام الحوادث بذاتِهِ العليَّةِ وتقريرهُ أنْ يُقالَ : لوِ اتَّصفَ تعالى بصفة حادثة لزمَ اتِّصافُهُ تعالى بالنقائص ، تعالى الله عن ذلكَ علوّاً كبيراً . وبيانُ الملازمة في ذلكَ : أنَّ تلك الصفة الحادثة التي فُرِضَ اتِّصافُهُ تعالى بها : إما أن تكون صفة نقص ، وإِمَّا أَنْ تكون صفة كمال فإنْ كانَتْ صفةَ نقص : فلزوم اتصافه تعالى بالنقص على تقدير اتّصافِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ بتلك الصفةِ الحادثة . . واضح البطلان . وإنْ كانَتْ صفةَ كمالٍ : لزمَ لفَرْضِ حدوثها ألا تكون ثابتة للذاتِ العليَّةِ في الأزلِ ؛ لمنافاة الحدوثِ للأزلِ ، فلزمَ إذاً أن تكونَ الذاتُ
[The third proof] And also: He, may He be glorified and exalted, is not described except with perfection by consensus. So it is necessary that this temporal attribute, which is assumed that He, exalted, is described by it, be from the attributes of perfection, yet it was absent from His sublime essence in pre-eternity, due to the assumption of its temporality. And the absence of perfection is a deficiency, and He, exalted, is declared free from it by the consensus of rational people. This is the third proof for the impossibility of the subsistence of temporal events in His sublime essence. Its clarification is that it is said: If the Exalted is described by a temporal attribute, then the Exalted would necessarily be described by deficiencies—exalted is Allah above that, a great exaltation. And the demonstration of the entailment in that is: That temporal attribute with which the Exalted is assumed to be described is either an attribute of deficiency or an attribute of perfection. If it is an attribute of deficiency, then the necessity of His being described with deficiency on the assumption of His being described by that temporal attribute is clearly false. And if it is an attribute of perfection, then due to the assumption of its temporality, it is necessary that it not be established for the sublime essence in pre-eternity, because temporality contradicts pre-eternity. So it is necessary then that the essence be...
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof (al-burhān al-thālith) for the impossibility of temporal accidents (ḥawādith) subsisting in the essence of Allah. The author begins by stating the premise: Allah is described only with perfection, by consensus. Then he argues that if we assume Allah is described by a temporal attribute (ṣifa ḥāditha), that attribute must be from the attributes of perfection (because He cannot be imperfect). However, being temporal, it was absent from His essence in pre-eternity. The absence of perfection is a deficiency (naqṣ), and Allah is free from all deficiency by consensus of rational people. The author then clarifies the entailment (mulāzama) using a dichotomy: that temporal attribute must be either a deficiency or a perfection. If it is a deficiency, then Allah would be described by deficiency, which is clearly false. If it is a perfection, then because it is temporal, it could not have been present in pre-eternity; but its absence would mean Allah lacked that perfection in eternity, which is a deficiency. Therefore, both possibilities lead to impossibility. The proof concludes that Allah cannot be described by any temporal attribute. The text as given is incomplete, cutting off mid-sentence after 'فلزم إذاً أن تكون الذات' (so it is necessary that the essence be...), but the conclusion has already been stated earlier: 'لزم اتصافه تعالى بالنقائص' (He would necessarily be described with deficiencies).

Key Terms
صفة كمال
صفة نقص
فوت الكمال
البرهان الثالث
ملازمة
حدوث
أزل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that God can acquire new perfections over time without deficiency.
Correction: This proof shows that any attribute He gains later must have been absent in pre-eternity, and absence of perfection is itself a deficiency—contradicting His perfect nature.

Checkpoint
What is the central dichotomy in the third proof?
A) The temporal attribute is either necessary or impossible.
B) The temporal attribute is either a perfection or a deficiency.
C) The temporal attribute is either eternal or temporal.
D) The temporal attribute is either essential or accidental.

Key Takeaway
The third proof shows that any temporal attribute of God would entail a deficiency, so God cannot be described by temporal attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

When you reflect on your own life, you find that you constantly change—sometimes better, sometimes worse. How does knowing that Allah is absolutely perfect and never changes impact your trust in Him? In what area of your life today do you need to remind yourself that Allah's perfection is eternal and unshakable?
?
You might sometimes imagine Allah's anger or pleasure as if He 'becomes' angry or 'becomes' pleased. Is this concept of change in Allah something your heart has secretly accepted? How does this lesson challenge that notion, and what can you do to correct your perception of Him?
?
Consider the attribute of mercy (rahma). It is a perfection. But if you think that Allah's mercy began when He created creation, that implies a lack of mercy before creation. Do you truly believe Allah's mercy is eternal and never absent? How should this affect your plea for mercy today?

Temporal Attributes Imply Deficiency
Sanusi restates the proof and answers a quick objection about successive attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why describing Allah with a temporal attribute necessarily implies deficiency, even if the attribute itself is one of perfection.

Core Idea
A temporal attribute means it was absent from Allah in pre-eternity, and that absence constitutes deficiency.

Sanusi has already established that a temporal attribute in Allah leads to deficiency, but the proof focused on the subtle case where the attribute is one of perfection. Here he clarifies the reasoning and preemptively dismisses a quick objection that might arise. The key point is that the attribute must have been absent in pre-eternity, and that absence is a deficiency.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two estimations
Sanusi explains that a temporal attribute could be deficient or perfect; the deficiency is obvious in the first case, so he only needed to prove the second.
2
Grasp the implication of perfection
Even if the temporal attribute is perfect, it must have been absent from Allah in pre-eternity, since it is temporal. Absence of perfection is itself a deficiency.
This is the core logical step.
3
Consider the immediate objection
An objector might say that Allah could have had similar attributes in succession without beginning, so no perfection is ever absent. Sanusi quickly dismisses this as an infinite regress, which is impossible.
This is a preview of the more detailed objection to come.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد بان لك بهذا : أنَّ اتصافَهُ تعالى بصفة حادثة يستلزم اتصافَهُ جل وعز بصفة نقص ، سواء قدَّرْتَ أنَّ تلك الصفة الحادثة صفةٌ نقص ، أو قدَّرْتَ أنَّها صفةٌ كمال . ولمَّا كانَ لزوم النقص على التقديرِ الأَوَّلِ جليّاً ، وعلى الثاني خفياً .. أضربنا في أصل العقيدة عن التقدير الأوَّلِ لوضوح لزومِ النقص معَهُ ، واقتصرنا على بيان الثاني لخفائه . فقوله : ( وقد فاتَتْ ذاتَهُ العليَّةَ في الأزلِ ) أي : أنَّ تلك الصفةَ الحادثة وإنْ كانَتْ صفة كمالٍ يلزمُ أنْ تفوت الذات في الأزلِ ؛ أي : لا تكون ثابتة لها فيهِ ؛ لاستحالة كون الحادثِ قديماً . ولا يُعترَضُ على هذا : بأنَّه لا يلزم منه فوتُ الذاتِ العليَّة كمال هذه الصفة الحادثة لاحتمال اتصافه بأمثالها على التوالي لا إلى أوَّلِ ؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : لا يخفى أنَّ هذا الاحتمال باطل ؛ لأنَّهُ تسلسلٌ مِنْ بابِ حوادث لا أَوَّلَ لها وهو ظاهر الاستحالة . هذا اعتراض على البرهان الثالث . و تقريرُهُ أَنْ يُقال : ما ذكرتموه مِنْ لزومِ النقص له تعالى على تقدير اتصافه تعالى بصفةٍ حادثة .. غيرُ مُسلَّم ، وقولكم في بيان لزوم ذلك : ( لأنَّ تلك الصفةَ لا بدَّ وأنْ تكون صفة كمال ، وقد فاتتِ الذات في الأزلِ ، وفوتُ الكمال نقص ) .. لا يصحُ ؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : لمَّا كانَتْ ذاتُهُ عزَّ وجلَّ أزليَّةً فما المانع أنْ يُقالَ باتصافه قبل تلك الصفة الحادثة المفروضة بأمثالها على التعاقبِ لا إلى أوَّلِ ، فلا يفوت حينئذ الذات كمال هذه الصفة - لا في الأزلِ ولا فيما لا يزالُ - حتى يلزم النقصُ ؟ والجواب عن هذا الاعتراض : ما أشرنا إليه في أصل العقيدة مراراً ؛ مِنْ أنَّ هذا الاحتمال الذي اعترض بهِ المعترِضُ على الدليل باطل قطعاً ؛ لأنَّ ذلك الاحتمال هو عين إثباتِ حوادث لا أَوَّلَ لها وقد سبق برهان استحالته .
This has made clear to you: that describing Him, exalted, with a temporal attribute necessarily entails describing Him, mighty and majestic, with an attribute of deficiency, whether you consider that temporal attribute to be an attribute of deficiency, or consider it to be an attribute of perfection. And since the necessity of deficiency on the first estimation is obvious, and on the second is subtle... we have omitted in the original creed the first estimation due to the clarity of the necessity of deficiency with it, and we restricted ourselves to explaining the second because of its subtlety. So His statement: (And His exalted essence was deprived of it in pre-eternity) means: that temporal attribute, even if it is an attribute of perfection, necessitates that it is absent from the essence in pre-eternity; i.e., it is not established for it therein, due to the impossibility of a temporal thing being eternal. And this is not objected to: that it does not necessarily entail the deprivation of the exalted essence of the perfection of this temporal attribute, due to the possibility of His being described with its likes in succession without beginning; because we say: it is not hidden that this possibility is invalid, because it is a regress of the category of temporal events without beginning, and it is manifestly impossible. This is an objection to the third proof. Its exposition is to say: What you have mentioned of the necessity of deficiency for Him, exalted, on the supposition of His being described with a temporal attribute... is not conceded, and your statement in explaining its necessity: (Because that attribute must be an attribute of perfection, and the essence was deprived of it in pre-eternity, and deprivation of perfection is deficiency)... is not correct; because we say: Since His essence, mighty and majestic, is eternal, what prevents it being said that He was described before that supposed temporal attribute with its likes in succession without beginning, so that then the essence is not deprived of the perfection of this attribute—neither in pre-eternity nor in what has no cessation—so that deficiency would necessarily arise? The answer to this objection: what we have indicated repeatedly in the original creed: that this possibility with which the objector has objected to the proof is absolutely invalid, because that possibility is precisely the affirmation of temporal events without beginning, and proof of its impossibility has already preceded.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to the third proof regarding God's temporal attributes and refutes it. The author first reiterates the conclusion: describing God with a temporal attribute necessarily implies deficiency, whether that attribute itself is deficient or perfect. The proof focused on the second case (attribute of perfection) because it is subtle. The reasoning is that a perfect attribute must have been absent from God in pre-eternity, and absence of perfection is deficiency. An immediate objection is raised: perhaps God can be described with successive similar perfect attributes without beginning, so no perfection is ever absent. The author quickly dismisses this as an infinite regress of temporal events, which is impossible. Then the objection is elaborated more formally: the objector denies the premise that deficiency necessarily follows, because God could have had similar attributes in succession. The author responds by referring back to the established proof that an infinite regress of temporal events is impossible. Thus the objection fails because it relies on an impossibility.

Key Terms
صفة حادثة
فوت الكمال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if an attribute is perfect, its temporality does not imply deficiency because it could have been absent in pre-eternity without issue.
Correction: Absence of a perfection in pre-eternity is itself a deficiency, so temporality always implies deficiency.

Checkpoint
Why did Sanusi focus on the case where the temporal attribute is one of perfection?
A) Because that case is the only one that occurs.
B) Because the deficiency in that case is subtle and needs proof.
C) Because the other case is impossible.
D) Because the objector only accepts perfect attributes.

Key Takeaway
Any temporal attribute in Allah implies deficiency, even if the attribute itself is perfect, because it was absent in pre-eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

When you think about Allah's attributes, do you ever unconsciously imagine Him acquiring new knowledge or power as events unfold? How does this lesson expose the deficiency in that thought, and what must you affirm instead about His eternal perfection?
?
Sanusi dismisses the objection of successive attributes as 'manifestly impossible.' Have you ever accepted a theological view just because it seemed convenient, without checking if it leads to an absurdity like infinite regress? What will you do to guard your faith against such false possibilities?
?
The subtlety of the second estimation (perfect temporal attribute) makes it easy to overlook. Can you identify any attribute you might wrongly consider 'temporal' in Allah under the guise of His responsiveness or mercy? What specific step will you take to purify your creed from this subtle deficiency?

Refuting the Formal Objection via Infinite Regress
Sanusi presents the formal objection and refutes it as an impossible infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the formal objection to the third proof and how Sanusi refutes it by appealing to the impossibility of an infinite regress of temporal events.

Core Idea
The objection's proposed succession of attributes without beginning is an infinite regress, which is impossible.

The previous lesson set up the quick dismissal of an objection. Now the objection is presented formally: the opponent argues that Allah could have been described with successive temporal attributes without beginning, so no perfection is ever absent. Sanusi responds by labeling this as an infinite regress of temporal events, which has already been proven impossible. This is a key moment in the proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the formal objection
The objector restates the proof and denies the premise, offering a scenario of successive attributes without beginning.
Note the language: 'what prevents...' is a rhetorical challenge.
2
Identify the key point of the objection
The objector claims that if attributes succeed each other endlessly, the essence is never deprived of perfection at any time, so no deficiency occurs.
3
Understand Sanusi's refutation
Sanusi says this scenario is exactly an infinite regress of temporal events, which has already been proven impossible in earlier discussions.
This refutation relies on a previous proof; no new argument is given here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد بان لك بهذا : أنَّ اتصافَهُ تعالى بصفة حادثة يستلزم اتصافَهُ جل وعز بصفة نقص ، سواء قدَّرْتَ أنَّ تلك الصفة الحادثة صفةٌ نقص ، أو قدَّرْتَ أنَّها صفةٌ كمال . ولمَّا كانَ لزوم النقص على التقديرِ الأَوَّلِ جليّاً ، وعلى الثاني خفياً .. أضربنا في أصل العقيدة عن التقدير الأوَّلِ لوضوح لزومِ النقص معَهُ ، واقتصرنا على بيان الثاني لخفائه . فقوله : ( وقد فاتَتْ ذاتَهُ العليَّةَ في الأزلِ ) أي : أنَّ تلك الصفةَ الحادثة وإنْ كانَتْ صفة كمالٍ يلزمُ أنْ تفوت الذات في الأزلِ ؛ أي : لا تكون ثابتة لها فيهِ ؛ لاستحالة كون الحادثِ قديماً . ولا يُعترَضُ على هذا : بأنَّه لا يلزم منه فوتُ الذاتِ العليَّة كمال هذه الصفة الحادثة لاحتمال اتصافه بأمثالها على التوالي لا إلى أوَّلِ ؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : لا يخفى أنَّ هذا الاحتمال باطل ؛ لأنَّهُ تسلسلٌ مِنْ بابِ حوادث لا أَوَّلَ لها وهو ظاهر الاستحالة . هذا اعتراض على البرهان الثالث . و تقريرُهُ أَنْ يُقال : ما ذكرتموه مِنْ لزومِ النقص له تعالى على تقدير اتصافه تعالى بصفةٍ حادثة .. غيرُ مُسلَّم ، وقولكم في بيان لزوم ذلك : ( لأنَّ تلك الصفةَ لا بدَّ وأنْ تكون صفة كمال ، وقد فاتتِ الذات في الأزلِ ، وفوتُ الكمال نقص ) .. لا يصحُ ؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : لمَّا كانَتْ ذاتُهُ عزَّ وجلَّ أزليَّةً فما المانع أنْ يُقالَ باتصافه قبل تلك الصفة الحادثة المفروضة بأمثالها على التعاقبِ لا إلى أوَّلِ ، فلا يفوت حينئذ الذات كمال هذه الصفة - لا في الأزلِ ولا فيما لا يزالُ - حتى يلزم النقصُ ؟ والجواب عن هذا الاعتراض : ما أشرنا إليه في أصل العقيدة مراراً ؛ مِنْ أنَّ هذا الاحتمال الذي اعترض بهِ المعترِضُ على الدليل باطل قطعاً ؛ لأنَّ ذلك الاحتمال هو عين إثباتِ حوادث لا أَوَّلَ لها وقد سبق برهان استحالته .
This has made clear to you: that describing Him, exalted, with a temporal attribute necessarily entails describing Him, mighty and majestic, with an attribute of deficiency, whether you consider that temporal attribute to be an attribute of deficiency, or consider it to be an attribute of perfection. And since the necessity of deficiency on the first estimation is obvious, and on the second is subtle... we have omitted in the original creed the first estimation due to the clarity of the necessity of deficiency with it, and we restricted ourselves to explaining the second because of its subtlety. So His statement: (And His exalted essence was deprived of it in pre-eternity) means: that temporal attribute, even if it is an attribute of perfection, necessitates that it is absent from the essence in pre-eternity; i.e., it is not established for it therein, due to the impossibility of a temporal thing being eternal. And this is not objected to: that it does not necessarily entail the deprivation of the exalted essence of the perfection of this temporal attribute, due to the possibility of His being described with its likes in succession without beginning; because we say: it is not hidden that this possibility is invalid, because it is a regress of the category of temporal events without beginning, and it is manifestly impossible. This is an objection to the third proof. Its exposition is to say: What you have mentioned of the necessity of deficiency for Him, exalted, on the supposition of His being described with a temporal attribute... is not conceded, and your statement in explaining its necessity: (Because that attribute must be an attribute of perfection, and the essence was deprived of it in pre-eternity, and deprivation of perfection is deficiency)... is not correct; because we say: Since His essence, mighty and majestic, is eternal, what prevents it being said that He was described before that supposed temporal attribute with its likes in succession without beginning, so that then the essence is not deprived of the perfection of this attribute—neither in pre-eternity nor in what has no cessation—so that deficiency would necessarily arise? The Unity of Each Divine Attribute
Sanusi argues that each of God's attributes must be singular, otherwise dualities would arise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why each of God's attributes of meaning must be singular and the rational proof behind that necessity.

Core Idea
God's attributes cannot be duplicated without absurdity.

Sanusi now addresses a subtle point about the divine attributes: not only are they eternal and distinct, but each attribute must also be singular. Could God have two knowledges or two powers? This short passage gives a crisp logical argument that He cannot, because that would lead to a contradiction. Let's read the proof carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a feel for its concise argument. Then read the literal English translation to understand the meaning.
Notice the title already sets the topic: 'The necessity of unity of attributes of meanings.'
2
Identify the claim and its proof
Sanusi states that each attribute must be one. Then he gives two impossible outcomes if it were not one: social al-mithlayn and tahseel al-hasil. Identify these terms.
3
Understand the two impossible outcomes
Break down what 'social al-mithlayn' (coexistence of two similars) and 'tahseel al-hasil' (attainment of the already attained) mean. Both are rationally impossible for God.
Use the commentary for clarification.
4
Apply the rule to all attributes of meaning
The passage ends by stating that this rule applies to every attribute that subsists in God's essence. That includes all seven attributes of meaning (knowledge, power, will, etc.).
Reflect on why this matters for understanding God's uniqueness.

وجوب الوحدة صفات المعاني ] يلزمُ أنْ تكونَ كلُّ صفةٍ مِنْ صفاتِهِ تعالى واحدةً ، وإلا لزم اجتماع المثلين ، وتحصيل الحاصل ، وهو محال . يعني : أنَّه يجبُ في كلِّ صفةٍ مِنَ الصفات التي تقوم بذاتِ مولانا .
The necessity of unity of attributes of meanings: It is necessary that every attribute of His, exalted, be one, otherwise there would result the coexistence of two similars, and the attainment of the already attained, and that is impossible. It means: that it is necessary regarding every attribute of the attributes that subsist in the essence of our Lord.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This short passage establishes a new rule: each of God's attributes (specifically attributes of meanings, like knowledge, power, will, etc.) must be singular, i.e., there cannot be two separate instances of the same attribute (e.g., two knowledges). The proof is that if there were two, they would either be exactly identical (attainment of the already attained, تحصيل الحاصل) or distinct but alike (coexistence of two similars, اجتماع المثلين), both of which are impossible in God. The explanation briefly states that this applies to every attribute that subsists in God's essence.

Key Terms
اجتماع المثلين
تحصيل الحاصل
صفات المعاني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God can have multiple instances of the same attribute (e.g., multiple knowledges) because His attributes are perfect.
Correction: Having two instances would either be two alike but distinct (social al-mithlayn) or identical (tahseel al-hasil), both impossible for God. Each attribute is one, not multiple.

Checkpoint
Why must each of God's attributes be one?
A) Because having two would imply limit in power.
B) Because otherwise there would be either two exactly alike or two identical, which is impossible.
C) Because attributes are not real.
D) Because God cannot have multiple attributes.

Key Takeaway
Each of God's attributes of meaning must be singular, because having two would lead to impossible redundancy or similarity.

?
The proof shows that two identical attributes would be redundant. Have you ever thought of God's mercy, for example, as having degrees or separate instances? How might that subtle thought imply imperfection in His mercy? Will you commit to purifying your belief, starting now, by affirming that each of His attributes is perfectly one?
?
Sanusi warns against imagining multiplicity in God's attributes. Is there any area of your life where you limit God by thinking He needs multiple attempts or multiple aspects to accomplish something? Right now, resolve to replace that doubt with the conviction that His singular, perfect attribute is enough.
